Capital of Turkey  
This article is about the Turkish capital city. For other uses, see [Ankara (disambiguation)](/wiki/Ankara_(disambiguation) "Ankara (disambiguation)").

<br />

Capital city and metropolitan municipality in Central Anatolia, Turkey

| Coordinates: [39°55′48″N 32°51′00″E﻿ / ﻿39.93000°N 32.85000°E﻿ / 39.93000; 32.85000](https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Ankara&params=39_55_48_N_32_51_00_E_region:TR_type:city(5864049)) ||

**Ankara** ^[\[b\]](#cite_note-16)^ is the [capital city](/wiki/Capital_city "Capital city") of [Turkey](/wiki/Turkey "Turkey"). Located in the [central part](/wiki/Central_Anatolia_Region "Central Anatolia Region") of [Anatolia](/wiki/Anatolia "Anatolia"), the city has a population of about 5.2 million in its urban center and about 5.8 million in [Ankara Province](/wiki/Ankara_Province "Ankara Province").^[\[5\]](#cite_note-Population_of_Turkey-6)^^[\[4\]](#cite_note-citypopulation.de-4)^ Ankara is Turkey's [second-largest city](/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Turkey "List of cities in Turkey") after [Istanbul](/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul") by population, first by urban area (4,130 km^2^), and third by metro area (25,632 km^2^) after [Konya](/wiki/Konya "Konya") and [Sivas](/wiki/Sivas "Sivas").{#cite_ref-citypopulation.de_4-2}

Serving as the capital of the ancient [Celtic](/wiki/Celts "Celts") state of [Galatia](/wiki/Galatia "Galatia") (280--64 BC), and later of the [Roman](/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire") province with the [same name](/wiki/Galatia_(Roman_province) "Galatia (Roman province)") (25 BC--7th century), Ankara has various [Hattian](/wiki/Hattians "Hattians"), [Hittite](/wiki/Hittites "Hittites"), [Lydian](/wiki/Lydia "Lydia"), [Phrygian](/wiki/Phrygia "Phrygia"), [Galatian](/wiki/Galatians_(people) "Galatians (people)"), [Greek](/wiki/Hellenistic_civilization "Hellenistic civilization"), [Persian](/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire "Achaemenid Empire"), [Roman](/wiki/Ancient_Rome "Ancient Rome"), [Byzantine](/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire"), and [Ottoman](/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") [archeological sites](/wiki/Archeological_site "Archeological site"). Ankara was historically known as Ancyra^[\[c\]](#cite_note-17)^ and Angora.^[\[d\]](#cite_note-19)^^[\[16\]](#cite_note-20)^ The Ottomans made the city the capital first of the [Anatolia Eyalet](/wiki/Anatolia_Eyalet "Anatolia Eyalet") (1393 -- late 15th century) and then the [Angora Eyalet](/wiki/Ankara_Eyalet "Ankara Eyalet") (1827--1864) and the [Angora Vilayet](/wiki/Angora_Vilayet "Angora Vilayet") (1867--1922).{#cite_ref-20}

The historical center of Ankara is a rocky hill rising 150 m (500 ft) over the left bank of the [Ankara River](/wiki/Ankara_River "Ankara River"), a tributary of the [Sakarya River](/wiki/Sakarya_River "Sakarya River"). The hill remains crowned by the ruins of [Ankara Castle](/wiki/Ankara_Castle "Ankara Castle"). Although few of its outworks have survived, there are well-preserved examples of [Roman](/wiki/Roman_architecture "Roman architecture") and [Ottoman architecture](/wiki/Ottoman_architecture "Ottoman architecture") throughout the city, the most remarkable being the 20 BC [Temple of Augustus and Rome](/wiki/Temple_of_Augustus_and_Rome "Temple of Augustus and Rome") that boasts the [Monumentum Ancyranum](/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum "Monumentum Ancyranum"), the inscription recording the *[Res Gestae Divi Augusti](/wiki/Res_Gestae_Divi_Augusti "Res Gestae Divi Augusti")*.^[\[17\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140–41-21)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140–41_21-0}

On 23 April 1920, the [Grand National Assembly of Turkey](/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey "Grand National Assembly of Turkey") was established in Ankara, which became the headquarters of the [Turkish National Movement](/wiki/Turkish_National_Movement "Turkish National Movement") during the [Turkish War of Independence](/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence "Turkish War of Independence"). Ankara became the new Turkish capital upon the establishment of the Republic on 29 October 1923, succeeding in this role as the former Turkish capital Istanbul following the [fall of the Ottoman Empire](/wiki/Defeat_and_dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Defeat and dissolution of the Ottoman Empire"). The [government](/wiki/Government_of_Turkey "Government of Turkey") is a prominent employer, but Ankara is also an important commercial and industrial city located at the center of Turkey's road and railway networks. The city gave its name to the [Angora wool](/wiki/Angora_wool "Angora wool") shorn from [Angora rabbits](/wiki/Angora_rabbit "Angora rabbit"), the long-haired [Angora goat](/wiki/Angora_goat "Angora goat") (the source of [mohair](/wiki/Mohair "Mohair")), and the [Angora cat](/wiki/Turkish_Angora "Turkish Angora"). The area is also known for its pears, honey and [Muscat](/wiki/Muscat_(grape) "Muscat (grape)") grapes. Although situated in one of the driest regions of Turkey and surrounded mostly by [steppe](/wiki/Steppe "Steppe") vegetation (except for the forested areas on the southern periphery), Ankara can be considered a [green city](/wiki/Green_city "Green city") in terms of green areas per inhabitant, at 72 square meters (775 square feet) per head.^[\[18\]](#cite_note-22)^{#cite_ref-22}  

Etymology {#Etymology}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: Etymology")\]

The orthography of the name *Ankara* ^[\[19\]](#cite_note-23)^ has varied over the ages. It has been identified with the [Hittite](/wiki/Hittites "Hittites") cult center *Ankuwaš*,^[\[20\]](#cite_note-qgmpff-24)^^[\[21\]](#cite_note-xtxpyw-25)^ although this remains a matter of debate.^[\[22\]](#cite_note-Gorny-26)^ In classical antiquity and during the medieval period, the city was known as *Ánkyra* (Ἄγκυρα,  '[anchor](/wiki/Anchor "Anchor")') in [Greek](/wiki/Ancient_Greek "Ancient Greek") and *Ancyra* in [Latin](/wiki/Latin "Latin"); the [Galatian Celtic](/wiki/Galatian_language "Galatian language") name was probably a similar variant. Following its annexation by the [Seljuk Turks](/wiki/Seljuk_Turks "Seljuk Turks") in 1073, the city became known in many European languages as *Angora* ; it was also known in [Ottoman Turkish](/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language "Ottoman Turkish language") as *Engürü* (انگورو).^[\[23\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaynes187845-27)^^[\[17\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140–41-21)^ The form "Angora" is preserved in the names of breeds of many different kinds of animals, and in the names of several locations in the US (see [Angora](/wiki/Angora_(disambiguation) "Angora (disambiguation)")).{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140–41_21-1}  

History {#History}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: History")\]  
Main article: [History of Ankara](/wiki/History_of_Ankara "History of Ankara")  
For a chronological guide, see [Timeline of Ankara](/wiki/Timeline_of_Ankara "Timeline of Ankara").

The region's history can be traced back to the [Bronze Age](/wiki/Bronze_Age "Bronze Age") [Hattic](/wiki/Hattians "Hattians") [civilization](/wiki/Hattic_language "Hattic language"), which was succeeded in the 2nd millennium BC by the [Hittites](/wiki/Hittites "Hittites"), in the 10th century BC by the [Phrygians](/wiki/Phrygia "Phrygia"), and later by the [Lydians](/wiki/Lydia "Lydia"), [Persians](/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire "Achaemenid Empire"), [Greeks](/wiki/Greeks "Greeks"), [Galatians](/wiki/Galatia "Galatia"), [Romans](/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire"), [Byzantines](/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire"), and [Turks](/wiki/Turkish_people "Turkish people") (the [Seljuk](/wiki/Great_Seljuq_Empire "Great Seljuq Empire") [Sultanate of Rûm](/wiki/Sultanate_of_R%C3%BBm "Sultanate of Rûm"), the [Ottoman Empire](/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") and finally republican [Türkiye](/wiki/Turkey "Turkey")).  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Alacastandarte_Hirsch%26L%C3%B6wen.jpg/200px-Alacastandarte_Hirsch%26L%C3%B6wen.jpg)](/wiki/File:Alacastandarte_Hirsch%26L%C3%B6wen.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/AlacaStandarte.jpg/200px-AlacaStandarte.jpg)](/wiki/File:AlacaStandarte.jpg)  
[Alaca Höyük bronze standards](/wiki/Alaca_H%C3%B6y%C3%BCk_bronze_standards "Alaca Höyük bronze standards") on display at the [Museum of Anatolian Civilizations](/wiki/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations "Museum of Anatolian Civilizations"), which is considered as the city's symbol.  

### Ancient history {#Ancient_history}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Ancient history")\]

The oldest settlements in and around the city center of Ankara belonged to the [Hattic](/wiki/Hattians "Hattians") [civilization](/wiki/Hattic_language "Hattic language") which existed during the [Bronze Age](/wiki/Bronze_Age "Bronze Age") and was gradually absorbed c. 2000 -- 1700 BC by the [Indo-European](/wiki/Hittite_language "Hittite language") [Hittites](/wiki/Hittites "Hittites"). The city grew significantly in size and importance under the [Phrygians](/wiki/Phrygia "Phrygia") starting around 1000 BC, and experienced a large expansion following the mass migration from [Gordion](/wiki/Gordium "Gordium"), (the capital of [Phrygia](/wiki/Phrygia "Phrygia")), after an earthquake which severely damaged that city around that time. In Phrygian tradition, King [Midas](/wiki/Midas "Midas") was venerated as the founder of Ancyra, but [Pausanias](/wiki/Pausanias_(geographer) "Pausanias (geographer)") mentions that the city was actually far older, which accords with present archeological knowledge.^[\[24\]](#cite_note-28)^{#cite_ref-28}

Phrygian rule was succeeded first by [Lydian](/wiki/Lydia "Lydia") and later by [Persian](/wiki/Iran "Iran") rule, though the strongly Phrygian character of the peasantry remained, as evidenced by the gravestones of the much later Roman period. Persian sovereignty lasted until the Persians' defeat at the hands of [Alexander the Great](/wiki/Alexander_the_Great "Alexander the Great") who conquered the city in 333 BC. Alexander came from [Gordion](/wiki/Gordium "Gordium") to Ankara and stayed in the city for a short period. After his death at [Babylon](/wiki/Babylon "Babylon") in 323 BC and the subsequent division of his empire among his generals, Ankara, and its environs fell into the share of [Antigonus](/wiki/Antigonus_I_Monophthalmus "Antigonus I Monophthalmus").

Another important expansion took place under the [Greeks](/wiki/Pontic_Greeks "Pontic Greeks") of [Pontos](/wiki/Pontus_(region) "Pontus (region)") who came there around 300 BC and developed the city as a trading center for the commerce of goods between the [Black Sea](/wiki/Black_Sea "Black Sea") ports and Crimea to the north; Assyria, Cyprus, and Lebanon to the south; and Georgia, Armenia and Persia to the east.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ By that time^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ the city also took its name Ἄγκυρα (*Ánkyra* , meaning *[anchor](/wiki/Anchor "Anchor")* in [Greek](/wiki/Greek_language "Greek language")) which, in slightly modified form, provides the modern name of *Ankara*.

  * [![Seated Woman of Çatalhöyük on display at the Museum of Anatolian Civilizations.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Seated_Woman_of_%C3%87atalh%C3%B6y%C3%BCk_on_black_background.jpg/90px-Seated_Woman_of_%C3%87atalh%C3%B6y%C3%BCk_on_black_background.jpg)](/wiki/File:Seated_Woman_of_%C3%87atalh%C3%B6y%C3%BCk_on_black_background.jpg "Seated Woman of Çatalhöyük on display at the Museum of Anatolian Civilizations.")  
  [Seated Woman of Çatalhöyük](/wiki/Seated_Woman_of_%C3%87atalh%C3%B6y%C3%BCk "Seated Woman of Çatalhöyük") on display at the [Museum of Anatolian Civilizations](/wiki/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations "Museum of Anatolian Civilizations").

### Celtic history {#Celtic_history}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: Celtic history")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Dying_gaul.jpg/220px-Dying_gaul.jpg)](/wiki/File:Dying_gaul.jpg) The *[Dying Galatian](/wiki/Dying_Galatian "Dying Galatian")* was a famous statue commissioned some time between 230 and 220 BC by King [Attalos I](/wiki/Attalus_I "Attalus I") of [Pergamon](/wiki/Pergamon "Pergamon") to honor his victory over the [Celtic](/wiki/Celts "Celts") [Galatians](/wiki/Galatia "Galatia") in [Anatolia](/wiki/Anatolia "Anatolia"). Roman marble copy of a [Hellenistic](/wiki/Hellenistic_civilization "Hellenistic civilization") work of the late 3rd century BC, at the [Capitoline Museums](/wiki/Capitoline_Museums "Capitoline Museums"), Rome.

In 278 BC, the city, along with the rest of central Anatolia, was occupied by a [Celtic](/wiki/Celts "Celts") group, the [Galatians](/wiki/Galatia "Galatia"), who were the first to make Ankara one of their main tribal centers, the headquarters of the [Tectosages](/wiki/Tectosages "Tectosages") tribe.^[\[25\]](#cite_note-29)^ Other centers were [Pessinus](/wiki/Pessinus "Pessinus"), today's Ballıhisar, for the [Trocmi](/wiki/Trocmi "Trocmi") tribe, and [Tavium](/wiki/Tavium "Tavium"), to the east of Ankara, for the [Tolistobogii](/wiki/Tolistobogii "Tolistobogii") tribe. The city was then known as *Ancyra* . The Celtic element was probably relatively small in numbers; a warrior aristocracy which ruled over [Phrygian](/wiki/Phrygian_language "Phrygian language")-speaking peasants. However, the [Celtic language](/wiki/Celtic_languages "Celtic languages") continued to be spoken in Galatia for many centuries. At the end of the 4th century, [St. Jerome](/wiki/Jerome "Jerome"), a native of Dalmatia, observed that the language spoken around Ankara was very similar to that being spoken in the northwest of the Roman world near [Trier](/wiki/Trier "Trier").{#cite_ref-29}  

### Roman history {#Roman_history}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: Roman history")\]

The city was subsequently passed under the control of the [Roman Empire](/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire"). In 25 BC, Emperor [Augustus](/wiki/Augustus "Augustus") raised it to the status of a *[polis](/wiki/Polis "Polis")* and made it the capital city of the [Roman province](/wiki/Roman_province "Roman province") of [Galatia](/wiki/Galatia_(Roman_province) "Galatia (Roman province)").^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ Ankara is famous for the *[Monumentum Ancyranum](/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum "Monumentum Ancyranum")* (*Temple of Augustus and Rome* ) which contains the official record of the *Acts of Augustus* , known as the *[Res Gestae Divi Augusti](/wiki/Res_Gestae_Divi_Augusti "Res Gestae Divi Augusti")* , an inscription cut in marble on the walls of this temple. The ruins of Ancyra still furnish today valuable [bas-reliefs](/wiki/Relief "Relief"), inscriptions and other architectural fragments. Two other Galatian tribal centers, [Tavium](/wiki/Tavium "Tavium") near [Yozgat](/wiki/Yozgat "Yozgat"), and [Pessinus](/wiki/Pessinus "Pessinus") (Balhisar) to the west, near Sivrihisar, continued to be reasonably important settlements in the Roman period, but it was Ancyra that grew into a grand metropolis.{#cite_ref-TIB_30-0}

An estimated 200,000 people lived in Ancyra in good times during the Roman Empire, a far greater number than was to be the case from after the fall of the Roman Empire until the early 20th century. The small [Ankara River](/wiki/Ankara_River "Ankara River") ran through the center of the Roman town. It has now been covered and diverted, but it formed the northern boundary of the old town during the Roman, Byzantine and Ottoman periods. Çankaya, the rim of the majestic hill to the south of the present city center, stood well outside the Roman city, but may have been a summer resort. In the 19th century, the remains of at least one [Roman villa](/wiki/Roman_villa "Roman villa") or large house were still standing not far from where the Çankaya Presidential Residence stands today. To the west, the Roman city extended until the area of the Gençlik Park and Railway Station, while on the southern side of the hill, it may have extended downward as far as the site presently occupied by [Hacettepe University](/wiki/Hacettepe_University "Hacettepe University"). It was thus a sizeable city by any standards and much larger than the Roman towns of [Gaul](/wiki/Gaul "Gaul") or [Britannia](/wiki/Britannia "Britannia").^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

Ancyra's importance rested on the fact that it was the junction point where the roads in northern Anatolia running north--south and east--west intersected, giving it major strategic importance for Rome's eastern frontier.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ The great imperial road running east passed through Ankara and a succession of emperors and their armies came this way. They were not the only ones to use the Roman highway network, which was equally convenient for invaders. In the second half of the 3rd century, Ancyra was invaded in rapid succession by the [Goths](/wiki/Goths "Goths") coming from the west (who rode far into the heart of [Cappadocia](/wiki/Cappadocia "Cappadocia"), taking slaves and pillaging) and later by the [Arabs](/wiki/Arab_people "Arab people"). For about a decade, the town was one of the western outposts of one of Palmyrean empress [Zenobia](/wiki/Zenobia "Zenobia") in the [Syrian Desert](/wiki/Syrian_Desert "Syrian Desert"), who took advantage of a period of weakness and disorder in the Roman Empire to set up a short-lived state of her own.{#cite_ref-TIB_30-1}

The town was reincorporated into the Roman Empire under Emperor [Aurelian](/wiki/Aurelian "Aurelian") in 272. The [tetrarchy](/wiki/Tetrarchy "Tetrarchy"), a system of multiple (up to four) emperors introduced by [Diocletian](/wiki/Diocletian "Diocletian") (284--305), seems to have engaged in a substantial program of rebuilding and of road construction from Ancyra westwards to Germe and [Dorylaeum](/wiki/Dorylaeum "Dorylaeum") (now [Eskişehir](/wiki/Eski%C5%9Fehir "Eskişehir")).

In its heyday, Roman Ancyra was a large market and trading center but it also functioned as a major administrative capital, where a high official ruled from the city's Praetorium, a large administrative palace or office. During the 3rd century, life in Ancyra, as in other Anatolian towns, seems to have become somewhat militarized in response to the invasions and instability of the town.

  Marble head of a Roman woman on display at the [Museum of Anatolian Civilizations](/wiki/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations "Museum of Anatolian Civilizations").
  * [![The Res Gestae Divi Augusti is the self-laudatory autobiography completed in 13 AD, just before his death, by the first Roman emperor Augustus. Most of the text is preserved on the walls of the Monumentum Ancyranum.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Res_Gestae.jpg/80px-Res_Gestae.jpg)](/wiki/File:Res_Gestae.jpg "The Res Gestae Divi Augusti is the self-laudatory autobiography completed in 13 AD, just before his death, by the first Roman emperor Augustus. Most of the text is preserved on the walls of the Monumentum Ancyranum.")  
  The *[Res Gestae Divi Augusti](/wiki/Res_Gestae_Divi_Augusti "Res Gestae Divi Augusti")* is the self-laudatory autobiography completed in 13 AD, just before his death, by the first [Roman emperor](/wiki/Roman_emperor "Roman emperor") [Augustus](/wiki/Augustus "Augustus"). Most of the text is preserved on the walls of the [Monumentum Ancyranum](/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum "Monumentum Ancyranum").
  * [![The Roman Baths of Ankara were constructed by the Roman emperor Caracalla (212–217) in honor of Asclepios, the God of Medicine, and built around three principal rooms: the caldarium (hot bath), the tepidarium (warm bath) and the frigidarium (cold bath) in a typically laid-out 80-by-120-meter (260-by-390-foot) classical complex.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Ankara_Thermen05.jpg/120px-Ankara_Thermen05.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_Thermen05.jpg "The Roman Baths of Ankara were constructed by the Roman emperor Caracalla (212–217) in honor of Asclepios, the God of Medicine, and built around three principal rooms: the caldarium (hot bath), the tepidarium (warm bath) and the frigidarium (cold bath) in a typically laid-out 80-by-120-meter (260-by-390-foot) classical complex.")  
  The [Roman Baths of Ankara](/wiki/Roman_Baths_of_Ankara "Roman Baths of Ankara") were constructed by the Roman emperor [Caracalla](/wiki/Caracalla "Caracalla") (212--217) in honor of [Asclepios](/wiki/Asclepios "Asclepios"), the God of Medicine, and built around three principal rooms: the *[caldarium](/wiki/Caldarium "Caldarium")* (hot bath), the *[tepidarium](/wiki/Tepidarium "Tepidarium")* (warm bath) and the *[frigidarium](/wiki/Frigidarium "Frigidarium")* (cold bath) in a typically laid-out 80-by-120-meter (260-by-390-foot) classical complex.

### Byzantine history {#Byzantine_history}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=6 "Edit section: Byzantine history")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/AnkaraColumnFar_c.JPG/150px-AnkaraColumnFar_c.JPG)](/wiki/File:AnkaraColumnFar_c.JPG) The *[Column of Julian](/wiki/Column_of_Julianus "Column of Julianus")* (362) was erected in honor of the Roman emperor [Julian the Apostate](/wiki/Julian_the_Apostate "Julian the Apostate")'s visit to Ancyra.

The city is well known during the 4th century as a center of Christian activity (see also [below](#Ecclesiastical_history)), due to frequent imperial visits, and through the letters of the pagan scholar [Libanius](/wiki/Libanius "Libanius").^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ Bishop [Marcellus of Ancyra](/wiki/Marcellus_of_Ancyra "Marcellus of Ancyra") and [Basil of Ancyra](/wiki/Basil_of_Ancyra "Basil of Ancyra") were active in the theological controversies of their day, and the city was the site of no fewer than three church synods in [314](/wiki/Synod_of_Ancyra "Synod of Ancyra"), 358 and 375, the latter two in favor of [Arianism](/wiki/Arianism "Arianism").^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^{#cite_ref-TIB_30-3}

The city was visited by Emperor [Constans I](/wiki/Constans_I "Constans I") (r. 337--350) in 347 and 350, [Julian](/wiki/Julian_(emperor) "Julian (emperor)") (r. 361--363) during his Persian campaign in 362, and Julian's successor [Jovian](/wiki/Jovian_(emperor) "Jovian (emperor)") (r. 363--364) in winter 363/364 (he entered his [consulship](/wiki/Roman_consul "Roman consul") while in the city). After Jovian's death soon after, [Valentinian I](/wiki/Valentinian_I "Valentinian I") (r. 364--375) was acclaimed emperor at Ancyra, and in the next year his brother [Valens](/wiki/Valens "Valens") (r. 364--378) used Ancyra as his base against the usurper [Procopius](/wiki/Procopius_(usurper) "Procopius (usurper)").^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ When the province of Galatia was divided sometime in 396/99, Ancyra remained the civil capital of Galatia I, as well as its ecclesiastical center ([metropolitan see](/wiki/Metropolitan_see "Metropolitan see")).^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ Emperor [Arcadius](/wiki/Arcadius "Arcadius") (r. 383--408) frequently used the city as his summer residence, and some information about the ecclesiastical affairs of the city during the early 5th century is found in the works of [Palladius of Galatia](/wiki/Palladius_of_Galatia "Palladius of Galatia") and Nilus of Ancyra.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^{#cite_ref-TIB_30-6}

In 479, the rebel [Marcian](/wiki/Marcian_(usurper) "Marcian (usurper)") attacked the city, without being able to capture it.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ In 610/11, [Comentiolus](/wiki/Comentiolus_(brother_of_Phocas) "Comentiolus (brother of Phocas)"), brother of Emperor [Phocas](/wiki/Phocas "Phocas") (r. 602--610), launched his own unsuccessful rebellion in the city against [Heraclius](/wiki/Heraclius "Heraclius") (r. 610--641).^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ Ten years later, in 620 or more likely 622, it was captured by the [Sassanid Persians](/wiki/Sassanid_Persia "Sassanid Persia") during the [Byzantine--Sassanid War of 602--628](/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Sassanid_War_of_602%E2%80%93628 "Byzantine–Sassanid War of 602–628"). Although the city returned to Byzantine hands after the end of the war, the [Persian](/wiki/Persians "Persians") presence left traces in the city's archeology, and likely began the process of its transformation from a [late antique](/wiki/Late_antique "Late antique") city to a medieval fortified settlement.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^{#cite_ref-TIB_30-9}

In 654, the city, also known in Arabic sources as *Qalat as-Salasil* ("fortress of the chains"),^[\[27\]](#cite_note-31)^ was captured for the first time by the [Arabs](/wiki/Arabs "Arabs") of the [Rashidun Caliphate](/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate "Rashidun Caliphate"), under [Muawiyah](/wiki/Mu%27awiya_I "Mu'awiya I"), the future founder of the [Umayyad Caliphate](/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate "Umayyad Caliphate").^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ At about the same time, the [themes](/wiki/Theme_(Byzantine_district) "Theme (Byzantine district)") were established in Anatolia, and Ancyra became capital of the [Opsician Theme](/wiki/Opsician_Theme "Opsician Theme"), which was the largest and most important theme until it was split up under Emperor [Constantine V](/wiki/Constantine_V "Constantine V") (r. 741--775); Ancyra then became the capital of the new [Bucellarian Theme](/wiki/Bucellarian_Theme "Bucellarian Theme").^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ The city was captured at least temporarily by the Umayyad prince [Maslama ibn Hisham](/wiki/Maslama_ibn_Hisham "Maslama ibn Hisham") in 739/40, the last of the Umayyads' territorial gains from the Byzantine Empire.^[\[28\]](#cite_note-32)^ Ancyra was attacked without success by [Abbasid](/wiki/Abbasid "Abbasid") forces in 776 and in 798/99. In 805, Emperor [Nikephoros I](/wiki/Nikephoros_I "Nikephoros I") (r. 802--811) strengthened its fortifications, a fact which probably saved it from sack during the [large-scale invasion](/wiki/Abbasid_invasion_of_Asia_Minor_(806) "Abbasid invasion of Asia Minor (806)") of Anatolia by Caliph [Harun al-Rashid](/wiki/Harun_al-Rashid "Harun al-Rashid") in the next year.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ Arab sources report that Harun and his successor [al-Ma'mun](/wiki/Al-Ma%27mun "Al-Ma'mun") (r. 813--833) took the city, but this information is later invention. In 838, however, during the [Amorium campaign](/wiki/Sack_of_Amorium "Sack of Amorium"), the armies of Caliph [al-Mu'tasim](/wiki/Al-Mu%27tasim "Al-Mu'tasim") (r. 833--842) converged and met at the city; abandoned by its inhabitants, Ancara was razed to the ground, before the Arab armies went on to besiege and destroy [Amorium](/wiki/Amorium "Amorium") reaching as far as [Smyrna](/wiki/Smyrna "Smyrna").^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ In 859, Emperor [Michael III](/wiki/Michael_III "Michael III") (r. 842--867) came to the city during a campaign against the Arabs, and ordered its fortifications restored.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ In 872, the city was menaced, but not taken, by the [Paulicians](/wiki/Paulicians "Paulicians") under [Chrysocheir](/wiki/Chrysocheir "Chrysocheir").^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ The last Arab raid to reach the city was undertaken in 931, by the Abbasid governor of [Tarsus](/wiki/Tarsus_(city) "Tarsus (city)"), [Thamal al-Dulafi](/wiki/Thamal_al-Dulafi "Thamal al-Dulafi"), but the city again was not captured.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^{#cite_ref-TIB_30-16}  

### Ecclesiastical history {#Ecclesiastical_history}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: Ecclesiastical history")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Teodot_Ankirski.jpg/160px-Teodot_Ankirski.jpg)](/wiki/File:Teodot_Ankirski.jpg) [St. Theodotus of Ancyra](/wiki/Theodotus_of_Ancyra_(martyr) "Theodotus of Ancyra (martyr)")

Early Christian martyrs of Ancyra, about whom little is known, included Proklos and Hilarios who were natives of the otherwise unknown nearby village of Kallippi, and suffered repression under the emperor [Trajan](/wiki/Trajan "Trajan") (98--117). In the 280s we hear of Philumenos, a Christian corn merchant from southern Anatolia, being captured and martyred in Ankara, and Eustathius.

As in other Roman towns, the reign of [Diocletian](/wiki/Diocletian "Diocletian") marked the culmination of the persecution of the Christians. In 303, Ancyra was one of the towns where the co-emperors Diocletian and his deputy [Galerius](/wiki/Galerius "Galerius") launched their anti-Christian persecution. In Ancyra, their first target was the 38-year-old Bishop of the town, whose name was Clement. Clement's life describes how he was taken to Rome, then sent back, and forced to undergo many interrogations and hardship before he, and his brother, and various companions were put to death. The remains of the church of [St. Clement](/wiki/Clement_of_Ancyra "Clement of Ancyra") can be found today in a building just off Işıklar Caddesi in the Ulus district. Quite possibly this marks the site where Clement was originally buried. Four years later, a doctor of the town named Plato and his brother Antiochus also became celebrated martyrs under Galerius. [Theodotus of Ancyra](/wiki/Theodotus_of_Ancyra_(martyr) "Theodotus of Ancyra (martyr)") is also venerated as a saint.

However, the persecution proved unsuccessful and in 314 Ancyra was the center of [an important council](/wiki/Synod_of_Ancyra "Synod of Ancyra") of the [early church](/wiki/Early_Christianity "Early Christianity");^[\[29\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERockwell1911-33)^ its 25 disciplinary canons constitute one of the most important documents in the early history of the administration of the [Sacrament of Penance](/wiki/Confession_(religion) "Confession (religion)").^[\[29\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERockwell1911-33)^ The synod also considered ecclesiastical policy for the reconstruction of the [Christian Church](/wiki/Christian_Church "Christian Church") after the persecutions, and in particular the treatment of *[lapsi](/wiki/Lapsi_(Christianity) "Lapsi (Christianity)")* ---Christians who had given in to forced [paganism](/wiki/Paganism "Paganism") (sacrifices) to avoid [martyrdom](/wiki/Martyrdom "Martyrdom") during these persecutions.^[\[29\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERockwell1911-33)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTERockwell1911_33-2}

Though paganism was probably tottering in Ancyra in Clement's day, it may still have been the majority religion. Twenty years later, Christianity and [monotheism](/wiki/Monotheism "Monotheism") had taken its place. Ancyra quickly turned into a Christian city, with a life dominated by monks and priests and theological disputes. The town council or senate gave way to the bishop as the main local figurehead. During the middle of the 4th century, Ancyra was involved in the complex theological disputes over the nature of Christ, and a form of [Arianism](/wiki/Arianism "Arianism") seems to have originated there.^[\[30\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParvis2006325–345-34)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParvis2006325–345_34-0}

In 362--363, Emperor Julian passed through Ancyra on his way to an ill-fated campaign against the Persians, and according to Christian sources, engaged in a persecution of various holy men.^[\[31\]](#cite_note-gibbon-35)^ The stone base for a statue, with an inscription describing Julian as "Lord of the whole world from the British Ocean to the barbarian nations", can still be seen, built into the eastern side of the inner circuit of the walls of Ankara Castle. The Column of Julian which was erected in honor of the emperor's visit to the city in 362 still stands today. In 375, Arian bishops met at Ancyra and deposed several bishops, among them [St. Gregory of Nyssa](/wiki/Gregory_of_Nyssa "Gregory of Nyssa").{#cite_ref-gibbon_35-0}

In the late 4th century, Ancyra became something of an imperial [holiday resort](/wiki/Resort "Resort"). After [Constantinople](/wiki/Constantinople "Constantinople") became the [East Roman](/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire") capital, emperors in the 4th and 5th centuries would retire from the humid summer weather on the [Bosporus](/wiki/Bosphorus "Bosphorus") to the drier mountain atmosphere of Ancyra. [Theodosius II](/wiki/Theodosius_II "Theodosius II") (408--450) kept his court in Ancyra in the summers. Laws issued in Ancyra testify to the time they spent there.

The [Metropolis of Ancyra](/wiki/Metropolis_of_Ancyra "Metropolis of Ancyra") continued to be a residential [see](/wiki/Episcopal_see "Episcopal see") of the [Eastern Orthodox Church](/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church "Eastern Orthodox Church") until the 20th century, with about 40,000 faithful, mostly Turkish-speaking, but that situation ended as a result of the 1923 [Convention Concerning the Exchange of Greek and Turkish Populations](/wiki/Convention_Concerning_the_Exchange_of_Greek_and_Turkish_Populations "Convention Concerning the Exchange of Greek and Turkish Populations"). The earlier [Armenian genocide](/wiki/Armenian_genocide "Armenian genocide") put an end to the residential eparchy of Ancyra of the [Armenian Catholic Church](/wiki/Armenian_Catholic_Church "Armenian Catholic Church"), which had been established in 1850.^[\[32\]](#cite_note-Bull_Universi_Dominici_gregis-36)^^[\[33\]](#cite_note-gallica.bnf.fr-37)^ It is also a titular metropolis of the [Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople](/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarchate_of_Constantinople "Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople").{#cite_ref-gallica.bnf.fr_37-0}

Both the Ancient Byzantine Metropolitan archbishopric and the 'modern' Armenian eparchy are now listed by the [Catholic Church](/wiki/Catholic_Church "Catholic Church") as [titular sees](/wiki/Titular_see "Titular see"),^[\[34\]](#cite_note-38)^ with separate [apostolic successions](/wiki/Apostolic_succession "Apostolic succession").{#cite_ref-38}  

### Seljuk and Ottoman history {#Seljuk_and_Ottoman_history}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: Seljuk and Ottoman history")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ottoman_Houses_Ankara.jpg/220px-Ottoman_Houses_Ankara.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ottoman_Houses_Ankara.jpg) Ottoman houses in Hamamönü district

After the [Battle of Manzikert](/wiki/Battle_of_Manzikert "Battle of Manzikert") in 1071, the [Seljuk Turks](/wiki/Seljuk_Turks "Seljuk Turks") overran much of Anatolia. By 1073, the Turkish settlers had reached the vicinity of Ancyra, and the city was captured shortly after, at the latest by the time of the rebellion of [Nikephoros Melissenos](/wiki/Nikephoros_Melissenos "Nikephoros Melissenos") in 1081.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ In 1101, when the [Crusade](/wiki/Crusade_of_1101 "Crusade of 1101") under [Raymond IV of Toulouse](/wiki/Raymond_IV_of_Toulouse "Raymond IV of Toulouse") arrived, the city had been under [Danishmend](/wiki/Danishmend "Danishmend") control for some time. The Crusaders captured the city, and handed it over to the Byzantine emperor [Alexios I Komnenos](/wiki/Alexios_I_Komnenos "Alexios I Komnenos") (r. 1081--1118).^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^ Byzantine rule did not last long, and the city was captured by the Seljuk [Sultanate of Rum](/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum "Sultanate of Rum") at some unknown point; in 1127, it returned to Danishmend control until 1143, when the Seljuks of Rum retook it.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-TIB-30)^{#cite_ref-TIB_30-19}

After the [Battle of Köse Dağ](/wiki/Battle_of_K%C3%B6se_Da%C4%9F "Battle of Köse Dağ") in 1243, in which the [Mongols](/wiki/Mongol_Empire "Mongol Empire") defeated the Seljuks, most of Anatolia became part of the dominion of the Mongols. Taking advantage of Seljuk decline, a semi-religious cast of craftsmen and trade people named *[Ahiler](/wiki/Ahis "Ahis")* chose Angora as their independent city-state in 1290. [Orhan](/wiki/Orhan "Orhan"), the second [Bey](/wiki/Bey "Bey") of the [Ottoman Empire](/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire"), captured the city in 1356. [Timur](/wiki/Timur "Timur") defeated [Bayezid I](/wiki/Bayezid_I "Bayezid I") at the [Battle of Ankara](/wiki/Battle_of_Ankara "Battle of Ankara") in 1402 and took the city, but in 1403 Angora was again under Ottoman control.

The [Levant Company](/wiki/Levant_Company "Levant Company") maintained a factory in the town from 1639 to 1768.^[\[17\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140–41-21)^ In the 19th century, its population was estimated at 20,000 to 60,000.^[\[23\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaynes187845-27)^ It was sacked by [Egyptians](/wiki/Khedivate_of_Egypt "Khedivate of Egypt") under [Ibrahim Pasha](/wiki/Ibrahim_Pasha_of_Egypt "Ibrahim Pasha of Egypt") in 1832.^[\[17\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140–41-21)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140–41_21-3}

From 1867 to 1922, the city served as the capital of the [Angora Vilayet](/wiki/Angora_Vilayet "Angora Vilayet"), which included most of ancient Galatia.

Prior to [World War I](/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"), the town had a [British](/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland "United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland") [consulate](/wiki/Consul_(representative) "Consul (representative)") and a population of around 28,000, roughly
1⁄3 of whom were Christian.^[\[17\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140–41-21)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140–41_21-4}  

### Turkish republican capital {#Turkish_republican_capital}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: Turkish republican capital")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Atat%C3%BCrk_TBMM%27den_%C3%A7%C4%B1karken.jpg/220px-Atat%C3%BCrk_TBMM%27den_%C3%A7%C4%B1karken.jpg)](/wiki/File:Atat%C3%BCrk_TBMM%27den_%C3%A7%C4%B1karken.jpg) President [Mustafa Kemal Atatürk](/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk "Mustafa Kemal Atatürk") (center) and Prime Minister [İsmet İnönü](/wiki/%C4%B0smet_%C4%B0n%C3%B6n%C3%BC "İsmet İnönü") (left) leaving the [Grand National Assembly of Türkiye](/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey "Grand National Assembly of Turkey") during the 7th anniversary celebrations of the Turkish Republic in 1930

Following the [Ottoman](/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") defeat in [World War I](/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"), the Ottoman capital [Constantinople](/wiki/Ottoman_Constantinople "Ottoman Constantinople") (modern Istanbul) and much of [Anatolia](/wiki/Anatolia "Anatolia") was occupied by the Allies, who planned to share these lands between [Armenia](/wiki/First_Republic_of_Armenia "First Republic of Armenia"), [France](/wiki/French_Third_Republic "French Third Republic"), [Greece](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Greece_(Gl%C3%BCcksburg) "Kingdom of Greece (Glücksburg)"), [Italy](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy "Kingdom of Italy") and the United Kingdom, leaving for the Turks the core piece of land in central Anatolia. In response, the leader of the Turkish nationalist movement, [Mustafa Kemal Atatürk](/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk "Mustafa Kemal Atatürk"), established the headquarters of his [resistance movement](/wiki/Turkish_National_Movement "Turkish National Movement") in Angora in 1920. After the [Turkish War of Independence](/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence "Turkish War of Independence") was won and the [Treaty of Sèvres](/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres "Treaty of Sèvres") was superseded by the [Treaty of Lausanne (1923)](/wiki/Treaty_of_Lausanne_(1923) "Treaty of Lausanne (1923)"), the Turkish nationalists replaced the Ottoman Empire with the [Republic of Turkey](/wiki/Republic_of_Turkey "Republic of Turkey") on 29 October 1923. A few days earlier, Angora had officially replaced Constantinople as the new Turkish capital city, on 13 October 1923,^[\[35\]](#cite_note-britannica-39)^ and Republican officials declared that the city's name is Ankara.^[\[36\]](#cite_note-40)^{#cite_ref-40}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Banks_Street_%28Atat%C3%BCrk_Boulevard%29_the_Building_of_Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1_%28Agricultural_Bank%29%2C_1930s_%2816851406391%29.jpg/220px-Banks_Street_%28Atat%C3%BCrk_Boulevard%29_the_Building_of_Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1_%28Agricultural_Bank%29%2C_1930s_%2816851406391%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Banks_Street_(Atat%C3%BCrk_Boulevard)_the_Building_of_Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1_(Agricultural_Bank),_1930s_(16851406391).jpg) A view of the old general directorate building of [Ziraat Bank](/wiki/Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1 "Ziraat Bankası"). It was designed by Istanbul-born [Italian Levantine](/wiki/Levantines_(Latin_Christians) "Levantines (Latin Christians)") architect Giulio Mongeri and built between 1926 and 1929.

After Ankara became the capital of the newly founded Republic of Turkey, new development divided the city into an old section, called *Ulus* , and a new section, called *Yenişehir* . Ancient buildings reflecting Roman, Byzantine, and Ottoman history and narrow winding streets mark the old section. The new section, now centered on [Kızılay Square](/wiki/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Meydan%C4%B1 "Kızılay Meydanı"), has the trappings of a more modern city: wide streets, hotels, theaters, shopping malls, and high-rises.

Government offices and foreign embassies are also located in the new section. Ankara has experienced a phenomenal growth since it was made Turkey's capital in 1923, when it was "a small town of no importance".^[\[37\]](#cite_note-41)^ In 1924, the year after the government had moved there, Ankara had about 35,000 residents. By 1927 there were 44,553 residents and by 1950 the population had grown to 286,781. After 1930, the city officially became known in Western languages as Ankara. By the late 1930s, the English name "Angora" was no longer in popular use.^[\[38\]](#cite_note-42)^{#cite_ref-42}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Library_Main_Hall_Columns.jpg/220px-Library_Main_Hall_Columns.jpg)](/wiki/File:Library_Main_Hall_Columns.jpg) The [Presidential Library](/wiki/Presidential_Library_(Turkey) "Presidential Library (Turkey)") in Ankara is the largest library in Turkey, with a collection of over 4 million printed books^[\[39\]](#cite_note-Presidential_Library-43)^ and over 120 million electronic editions^[\[39\]](#cite_note-Presidential_Library-43)^ published in 134 languages.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-Presidential_Library-43)^

Ankara continued to grow rapidly during the latter half of the 20th century and eventually outranked [İzmir](/wiki/%C4%B0zmir "İzmir") as Turkey's second-largest city, after [Istanbul](/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul"). Ankara's urban population reached 4,587,558 in 2014, while the population of [Ankara Province](/wiki/Ankara_Province "Ankara Province") reached 5,150,072 in 2015.^[\[40\]](#cite_note-citypopulation1-44)^{#cite_ref-citypopulation1_44-0}

The [Presidential Palace of Türkiye](/wiki/Presidential_Complex_(Turkey) "Presidential Complex (Turkey)") is situated in Ankara. This building serves as the main residence of the president.  

Geography {#Geography}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: Geography")\]  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Koppen-Geiger_Map_TUR_present_with_provinces.svg/2500px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_TUR_present_with_provinces.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_TUR_present_with_provinces.svg "Köppen map of Ankara Province and surrounding regions:[41]   BSk   Csb   Dfb   Dsb")  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Koppen-Geiger_Map_TUR_present_with_provinces.svg/2500px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_TUR_present_with_provinces.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_TUR_present_with_provinces.svg)  
[](/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_TUR_present_with_provinces.svg "File:Koppen-Geiger Map TUR present with provinces.svg")
Köppen map of Ankara Province and surrounding regions:^[\[41\]](#cite_note-45)^  
*  
  [BSk](/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate "Cold semi-arid climate")
*  
  [Csb](/wiki/Warm-summer_Mediterranean_climate "Warm-summer Mediterranean climate")
*  
  [Dfb](/wiki/Humid_continental_climate "Humid continental climate")
*  
  [Dsb](/wiki/Humid_continental_climate "Humid continental climate")

Geographically, Ankara is located in the middle of the [Kızılırmak](/wiki/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1l%C4%B1rmak_River "Kızılırmak River") and [Sakarya](/wiki/Sakarya_River "Sakarya River") rivers, and the [Sakarya River](/wiki/Sakarya_River "Sakarya River") forms its border with [Eskişehir](/wiki/Eski%C5%9Fehir "Eskişehir") in the west. Ankara shares its borders with [Bolu](/wiki/Bolu "Bolu") and [Çankırı](/wiki/%C3%87ank%C4%B1r%C4%B1 "Çankırı") in the north; [Konya](/wiki/Konya "Konya") in the south and [Kırıkkale](/wiki/K%C4%B1r%C4%B1kkale "Kırıkkale") in the east.^[\[42\]](#cite_note-46)^{#cite_ref-46}

Ankara and [its province](/wiki/Ankara_Province "Ankara Province") are located in the [Central Anatolia Region](/wiki/Central_Anatolia_Region "Central Anatolia Region") of Turkey. The Çubuk Brook flows through the city center of Ankara. It is connected in the western suburbs of the city to the [Ankara River](/wiki/Ankara_River "Ankara River"), which is a [tributary](/wiki/Tributary "Tributary") of the [Sakarya River](/wiki/Sakarya_River "Sakarya River").  

### Climate {#Climate}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Climate")\]

Ankara has a [cold semi-arid climate](/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate "Cold semi-arid climate") under the [Köppen climate classification](/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification") (*BSk* ), while under the [Trewartha climate classification](/wiki/Trewartha_climate_classification "Trewartha climate classification"), the city is classified as [humid continental](/wiki/Humid_continental_climate "Humid continental climate") (*Dc* ). Due to its elevation and inland location, Ankara has cold and snowy winters, and hot and dry summers. Rainfall occurs mostly during the spring and autumn. The city lies in [USDA](/wiki/USDA "USDA") [Hardiness zone](/wiki/Hardiness_zone "Hardiness zone") 7b, and its annual average precipitation is fairly low at 414 millimeters (16 in), nevertheless precipitation can be observed throughout the year. Monthly mean temperatures range from 0.9 °C (33.6 °F) in January to 24.3 °C (75.7 °F) in July, with an annual mean of 12.6 °C (54.7 °F).^[\[43\]](#cite_note-eather1-47)^ Ankara's overall temperature regime is very similar to [New York City](/wiki/New_York_City "New York City").{#cite_ref-eather1_47-0}  
{#cite_ref-eather1_47-1}{#cite_ref-WMOCLINO_48-0}
