Demographics {#Demographics}
----------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Demographics")\]
{#cite_ref-tuik_49-0}

| Year |           |        |
| 2007 | 4,466,756 |  ---   |
| 2012 | 4,965,542 | +2.14% |
| 2017 | 5,445,026 | +1.86% |
| 2022 | 5,782,285 | +1.21% |
|------|-----------|--------|
| Source: [TÜİK](/wiki/Turkish_Statistical_Institute "Turkish Statistical Institute")^[\[45\]](#cite_note-tuik-49)^ |||
[Historical population]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Ankara_road_map.png/220px-Ankara_road_map.png)](/wiki/File:Ankara_road_map.png) Ankara [metropolitan area](/wiki/Metropolitan_area "Metropolitan area")

Ankara had a population of 75,000 in 1927. There were 74,632 male residents and 48,882 female residents in Ankara according to the 1935 census.^[\[46\]](#cite_note-50)^ As of 2022, the population of the Ankara Province was 5,782,285.^[\[45\]](#cite_note-tuik-49)^ When Ankara became the capital of the Republic of Turkey in 1923, it was designated as a planned city for 500,000 future inhabitants. During the 1920s, 1930s and 1940s, the city grew in a planned and orderly pace. However, from the 1950s onward, the city grew much faster than envisioned, because unemployment and poverty forced people to migrate from the countryside into the city to seek a better standard of living. As a result, many illegal houses called [gecekondu](/wiki/Gecekondu "Gecekondu") were built around the city, causing the unplanned and uncontrolled urban landscape of Ankara, as not enough planned housing could be built fast enough. Although precariously built, the vast majority of them have electricity, running water and modern household amenities.{#cite_ref-tuik_49-1}

Nevertheless, many of these gecekondus have been replaced by huge public housing projects in the form of [tower blocks](/wiki/Tower_block "Tower block") such as Elvankent, [Eryaman](/wiki/Eryaman,_Etimesgut "Eryaman, Etimesgut") and [Güzelkent](/wiki/G%C3%BCzelkent,_Etimesgut "Güzelkent, Etimesgut"); and also as mass housing compounds for military and civil service accommodation. Although many gecekondus still remain, they too are gradually being replaced by mass housing compounds, as empty land plots in the city of Ankara for new construction projects are becoming impossible to find.

Çorum and Yozgat, which are located in Central Anatolia and whose population is decreasing, are the provinces with the highest net migration to Ankara.^[\[47\]](#cite_note-51)^ About one third of the Central Anatolia population of 15,608,868 people resides in Ankara.{#cite_ref-51}

The [literacy rate](/wiki/Literacy_rate "Literacy rate") in the whole province for people who are 15 years old or older is 98.18% according to 2020 TÜİK data. Ankara Province also has the highest percentage of tertiary education graduates in Turkey with 29.08% of the population having either an undergraduate, master's or doctor's degree.^[\[48\]](#cite_note-52)^{#cite_ref-52}  

Economy and infrastructure {#Economy_and_infrastructure}
--------------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: Economy and infrastructure")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Yda_Ankara_2024.jpg/250px-Yda_Ankara_2024.jpg)](/wiki/File:Yda_Ankara_2024.jpg) YDA Center in [Söğütözü](/wiki/S%C3%B6%C4%9F%C3%BCt%C3%B6z%C3%BC "Söğütözü"), Ankara

Ankara has long been a productive agricultural region in Anatolia. In the Ottoman period, Ankara was well known for producing grain, cotton, and fruits.^[\[49\]](#cite_note-53)^{#cite_ref-53}

The city has exported [mohair](/wiki/Mohair "Mohair") (from the [Angora goat](/wiki/Angora_goat "Angora goat")) and [Angora wool](/wiki/Angora_wool "Angora wool") (from the [Angora rabbit](/wiki/Angora_rabbit "Angora rabbit")) internationally for centuries. In the 19th century, the city also exported substantial amounts of [goat](/wiki/Goatskin_(material) "Goatskin (material)") and cat skins, [gum](/wiki/Gum_arabic "Gum arabic"), [wax](/wiki/Beeswax "Beeswax"), [honey](/wiki/Honey "Honey"), berries, and [madder root](/wiki/Madder_root "Madder root").^[\[23\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaynes187845-27)^ It was connected to [Istanbul](/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul") by railway before the [First World War](/wiki/First_World_War "First World War"), continuing to export mohair, wool, berries, and grain.^[\[17\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140–41-21)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140–41_21-5}

The [Central Anatolia Region](/wiki/Central_Anatolia_Region "Central Anatolia Region") is one of the primary locations of grape and [wine production in Turkey](/wiki/Turkish_wine "Turkish wine"), and Ankara is particularly famous for its [Kalecik Karası](/wiki/Kalecik_Karas%C4%B1 "Kalecik Karası") and [Muscat grapes](/wiki/Muscat_(grape_and_wine) "Muscat (grape and wine)"); and its [Kavaklıdere wine](/wiki/Kavakl%C4%B1dere_(winery) "Kavaklıdere (winery)"), which is produced in the [Kavaklıdere](/wiki/Kavakl%C4%B1dere,_Ankara "Kavaklıdere, Ankara") neighborhood within the [Çankaya](/wiki/%C3%87ankaya,_Ankara "Çankaya, Ankara") district of the city. Ankara is also famous for its pears. Another natural product of Ankara is its indigenous type of [honey](/wiki/Honey "Honey") (*Ankara Balı* ) which is known for its light color and is mostly produced by the [Atatürk Forest Farm and Zoo](/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk_Forest_Farm_and_Zoo "Atatürk Forest Farm and Zoo") in the Gazi district, and by other facilities in the Elmadağ, Çubuk and Beypazarı districts. [Çubuk-1](/wiki/%C3%87ubuk-1_Dam "Çubuk-1 Dam") and [Çubuk-2](/wiki/%C3%87ubuk-2_Dam "Çubuk-2 Dam") dams on the Çubuk Brook in Ankara were among the first dams constructed in the Turkish Republic.
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square_001.jpg/250px-K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square_001.jpg)](/wiki/File:K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square_001.jpg) [Kızılay Square](/wiki/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square "Kızılay Square") and [Emek Business Center](/wiki/Kahramanlar_Business_Center "Kahramanlar Business Center") (1959--1965), the first [International Style](/wiki/International_Style_(architecture) "International Style (architecture)") office tower and shopping center in Turkey.^[\[50\]](#cite_note-54)^^[\[51\]](#cite_note-55)^

Ankara is the center of the state-owned and private Turkish [defence](/wiki/Arms_industry "Arms industry") and [aerospace](/wiki/Aerospace_manufacturer "Aerospace manufacturer") companies, where the industrial plants and headquarters of the [Turkish Aerospace Industries](/wiki/Turkish_Aerospace_Industries "Turkish Aerospace Industries"), [MKE](/wiki/Mechanical_and_Chemical_Industry_Corporation_(Turkey) "Mechanical and Chemical Industry Corporation (Turkey)"), [ASELSAN](/wiki/ASELSAN "ASELSAN"), [HAVELSAN](/wiki/HAVELSAN "HAVELSAN"), [ROKETSAN](/wiki/ROKETSAN "ROKETSAN"), [FNSS](/wiki/FNSS_Defence_Systems "FNSS Defence Systems"),^[\[52\]](#cite_note-56)^ [Nurol Makina](/wiki/Nurol_Makina "Nurol Makina"),^[\[53\]](#cite_note-57)^ and numerous other firms are located. Exports to foreign countries from these defense and aerospace firms have steadily increased in the past decades. The [IDEF](/wiki/International_Defence_Industry_Fair "International Defence Industry Fair") in Ankara is one of the largest international expositions of the global [arms industry](/wiki/Arms_industry "Arms industry"). A number of the global [automotive companies](/wiki/Automotive_industry "Automotive industry") also have production facilities in Ankara, such as the German bus and truck manufacturer [MAN SE](/wiki/MAN_SE "MAN SE").^[\[54\]](#cite_note-58)^ Ankara hosts the [OSTIM Industrial Zone](/wiki/OSTIM_Industrial_Zone "OSTIM Industrial Zone"), Turkey's largest [industrial park](/wiki/Industrial_park "Industrial park").{#cite_ref-58}

A large percentage of the complicated employment in Ankara is provided by the state institutions; such as the [ministries](/wiki/Ministry_(government_department) "Ministry (government department)"), subministries, and other administrative bodies of the Turkish government. There are also many foreign citizens working as diplomats or clerks in the [embassies](/wiki/Embassy "Embassy") of their respective countries.  

Transportation {#Transportation}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: Transportation")\]  
See also: [Ankara Metro](/wiki/Ankara_Metro "Ankara Metro"), [Ankara railway station](/wiki/Ankara_railway_station "Ankara railway station"), [Ankara Esenboğa Airport](/wiki/Ankara_Esenbo%C4%9Fa_Airport "Ankara Esenboğa Airport"), and [List of airports in Ankara](/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Ankara "List of airports in Ankara")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Ankara_asv2021-10_img19_Railway_station.jpg/220px-Ankara_asv2021-10_img19_Railway_station.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_asv2021-10_img19_Railway_station.jpg) [Ankara railway station](/wiki/Ankara_railway_station "Ankara railway station") is a hub for conventional trains. [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Ankara_Tren_Gar%C4%B1.jpg/220px-Ankara_Tren_Gar%C4%B1.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_Tren_Gar%C4%B1.jpg) The new [ATG terminal](/wiki/Ankara_Tren_Gar%C4%B1 "Ankara Tren Garı") is a hub for the [high-speed rail](/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Turkey "High-speed rail in Turkey") ([YHT](/wiki/Y%C3%BCksek_H%C4%B1zl%C4%B1_Tren "Yüksek Hızlı Tren")) services.

The *Electricity, Gas, Bus General Directorate* (EGO)^[\[55\]](#cite_note-59)^ operates the [Ankara Metro](/wiki/Ankara_Metro "Ankara Metro") and other forms of public transportation. Ankara is served by a [suburban rail](/wiki/Commuter_rail "Commuter rail") named [Başkentray](/wiki/Ba%C5%9Fkentray "Başkentray") (B1) and five [Metro](/wiki/Rapid_transit "Rapid transit") lines (A1, M1, M2, M3, M4) of the Ankara Metro with about 400,000 total daily commuters, while additional subway lines (A2 and M2a/b) are under construction. A 3.2 km (2.0 mi) long [gondola lift](/wiki/Gondola_lift "Gondola lift") with four stations connects the district of Şentepe to the [Yenimahalle metro station](/wiki/Yenimahalle "Yenimahalle").^[\[56\]](#cite_note-60)^{#cite_ref-60}

[Ankara Central Station](/wiki/Ankara_railway_station "Ankara railway station") is a major rail hub in Turkey. The [Turkish State Railways](/wiki/Turkish_State_Railways "Turkish State Railways") operates passenger train service from Ankara to other major cities, such as: [Istanbul](/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul"), [Eskişehir](/wiki/Eski%C5%9Fehir "Eskişehir"), [Balıkesir](/wiki/Bal%C4%B1kesir "Balıkesir"), [Kütahya](/wiki/K%C3%BCtahya "Kütahya"), [İzmir](/wiki/%C4%B0zmir "İzmir"), [Kayseri](/wiki/Kayseri "Kayseri"), [Adana](/wiki/Adana "Adana"), [Kars](/wiki/Kars "Kars"), [Elazığ](/wiki/Elaz%C4%B1%C4%9F "Elazığ"), [Malatya](/wiki/Malatya "Malatya"), [Diyarbakır](/wiki/Diyarbak%C4%B1r "Diyarbakır"), [Karabük](/wiki/Karab%C3%BCk "Karabük"), [Zonguldak](/wiki/Zonguldak "Zonguldak") and [Sivas](/wiki/Sivas "Sivas"). Commuter rail also runs between the stations of [Sincan and Kayaş](/wiki/Sincan-Kaya%C5%9F_Line "Sincan-Kayaş Line"). On 13 March 2009, the new [Yüksek Hızlı Tren](/wiki/Y%C3%BCksek_H%C4%B1zl%C4%B1_Tren "Yüksek Hızlı Tren") (YHT) [high-speed rail service](/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Turkey "High-speed rail in Turkey") began operation between Ankara and Eskişehir. On 23 August 2011, another YHT high-speed line commercially started its service [between Ankara and Konya](/wiki/Ankara-Konya_high-speed_railway "Ankara-Konya high-speed railway"). On 25 July 2014, the [Ankara--Istanbul high-speed line](/wiki/Ankara-Istanbul_high-speed_railway "Ankara-Istanbul high-speed railway") of YHT entered service.^[\[57\]](#cite_note-61)^{#cite_ref-61}

[Ankara Esenboğa Airport](/wiki/Ankara_Esenbo%C4%9Fa_Airport "Ankara Esenboğa Airport"), located in the north-east of the city, is Ankara's main airport. Whilst the [AŞTİ](/wiki/A%C5%9ET%C4%B0 "AŞTİ") is the main coach terminal.  

### Ankara public transportation statistics {#Ankara_public_transportation_statistics}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Ankara public transportation statistics")\]

The average amount of time people spend commuting on public transit in Ankara on a weekday is 71 minutes. 17% of public transit passengers, ride for more than two hours every day. The average amount of time people wait at a stop or station for public transit is sixteen minutes, while 28% of users wait for over twenty minutes on average every day. The average distance people usually ride in a single trip with public transit is 9.9 km (6.2 mi), while 27% travel for over 12 km (7.5 mi) in a single direction.^[\[58\]](#cite_note-62)^{#cite_ref-62}  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Esenboga_International_Airport_Ankara_Turkey.jpg/600px-Esenboga_International_Airport_Ankara_Turkey.jpg)](/wiki/File:Esenboga_International_Airport_Ankara_Turkey.jpg "Esenboğa International Airport")  
[](/wiki/File:Esenboga_International_Airport_Ankara_Turkey.jpg "File:Esenboga International Airport Ankara Turkey.jpg")
[Esenboğa International Airport](/wiki/Esenbo%C4%9Fa_International_Airport "Esenboğa International Airport")  

Politics {#Politics}
--------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Politics")\]  
See also: [List of mayors of Ankara](/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Ankara "List of mayors of Ankara")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Ankara_local_elections_2019.png/175px-Ankara_local_elections_2019.png)](/wiki/File:Ankara_local_elections_2019.png) [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Mansur_Yava%C5%9F_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Mansur_Yava%C5%9F_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Mansur_Yava%C5%9F_(cropped).jpg) [Mansur Yavaş](/wiki/Mansur_Yava%C5%9F "Mansur Yavaş") of the [CHP](/wiki/Republican_People%27s_Party "Republican People's Party") is the Mayor of Ankara.

Since 8 April 2019, the mayor of Ankara is [Mansur Yavaş](/wiki/Mansur_Yava%C5%9F "Mansur Yavaş") from the [Republican People's Party](/wiki/Republican_People%27s_Party "Republican People's Party") (CHP), who won the [mayoral election in 2019](/wiki/2019_Ankara_mayoral_election "2019 Ankara mayoral election") and [2024](/wiki/2024_Ankara_mayoral_election "2024 Ankara mayoral election").

Ankara is politically a triple battleground between the ruling conservative [AK Party](/wiki/AK_Party "AK Party"), the opposition [Kemalist](/wiki/Kemalism "Kemalism") center-left [Republican People's Party](/wiki/Republican_People%27s_Party "Republican People's Party") (CHP) and the nationalist far-right [MHP](/wiki/Nationalist_Movement_Party "Nationalist Movement Party"). The [province of Ankara](/wiki/Ankara_Province "Ankara Province") is divided into 25 districts. Historically, the CHP's key and almost only political stronghold in Ankara lied within the central area of [Çankaya](/wiki/%C3%87ankaya,_Ankara_(district) "Çankaya, Ankara (district)"), which is the city's most populous district. While the CHP has always gained between 60 and 70% of the vote in Çankaya since 2002, political support elsewhere throughout Ankara was minimal. The high population within Çankaya, as well as [Yenimahalle](/wiki/Yenimahalle "Yenimahalle") to an extent, has allowed the CHP to take overall second place behind the AK Party in both local and general elections, with the MHP a close third, despite the fact that the MHP was politically stronger than the CHP in almost every other district. Overall, the AK Party enjoyed the most support throughout the city. The electorate of Ankara thus tended to vote in favor of the political right, far more so than the other main cities of [Istanbul](/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul") and [İzmir](/wiki/%C4%B0zmir "İzmir"). In retrospect, the [2013--14 protests against the AK Party government](/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_protests_in_Turkey "2013–14 protests in Turkey") were particularly strong in Ankara, proving to be fatal on multiple occasions.^[\[59\]](#cite_note-63)^{#cite_ref-63}

| Ankara district Municipalities [Local elections, 2024](/wiki/2024_Ankara_mayoral_election "2024 Ankara mayoral election") ||
| [CHP](/wiki/Republican_People%27s_Party "Republican People's Party") | 16 / 25 |
|                [AK Party](/wiki/AK_Party "AK Party")                 | 8 / 25  |
|                             Independent                              | 1 / 25  |
|----------------------------------------------------------------------|---------|

The city suffered from a series of terrorist attacks in 2015 and 2016, most notably on [10 October 2015](/wiki/2015_Ankara_bombings "2015 Ankara bombings"); [17 February 2016](/wiki/February_2016_Ankara_bombing "February 2016 Ankara bombing"); and [13 March 2016](/wiki/March_2016_Ankara_bombing "March 2016 Ankara bombing"). The city was also one of the sites of the [coup](/wiki/2016_Turkish_coup_attempt "2016 Turkish coup attempt") attempt on 15 July 2016.

[Melih Gökçek](/wiki/Melih_G%C3%B6k%C3%A7ek "Melih Gökçek") was the Metropolitan Mayor of Ankara between 1994 and 2017. Initially elected in the [1994 local elections](/wiki/1994_Turkish_local_elections "1994 Turkish local elections"), he was re-elected in [1999](/wiki/1999_Turkish_local_elections "1999 Turkish local elections"), [2004](/wiki/2004_Turkish_local_elections "2004 Turkish local elections") and [2009](/wiki/2009_Turkish_local_elections "2009 Turkish local elections"). In the [2014 local elections](/wiki/2014_Turkish_local_elections "2014 Turkish local elections"), Gökçek stood for a fifth term. The MHP's metropolitan mayoral candidate for the 2009 local elections, [Mansur Yavaş](/wiki/Mansur_Yava%C5%9F "Mansur Yavaş"), stood as the CHP's candidate against Gökçek in 2014. In a heavily controversial election, Gökçek was declared the winner by just 1% ahead of Yavaş amid allegations of systematic electoral fraud. With the [Supreme Electoral Council](/wiki/Supreme_Election_Council_(Turkey) "Supreme Election Council (Turkey)") and courts rejecting his appeals, Yavaş declared his intention to take the irregularities to the [European Court of Human Rights](/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights "European Court of Human Rights"). Although Gökçek was inaugurated for a fifth term, most election observers believe^[\[60\]](#cite_note-64)^ that Yavaş was the winner of the election.^[\[61\]](#cite_note-65)^^[\[62\]](#cite_note-66)^^[\[63\]](#cite_note-67)^^[\[64\]](#cite_note-68)^^[\[65\]](#cite_note-69)^ Gökçek resigned on 28 October 2017 and was replaced by the former mayor of [Sincan](/wiki/Sincan,_Ankara "Sincan, Ankara") district, [Mustafa Tuna](/wiki/Mustafa_Tuna "Mustafa Tuna"); who was succeeded by [Mansur Yavaş](/wiki/Mansur_Yava%C5%9F "Mansur Yavaş") of the [CHP](/wiki/Republican_People%27s_Party "Republican People's Party"), the current mayor of Ankara, [elected in 2019](/wiki/2019_Ankara_mayoral_election "2019 Ankara mayoral election").{#cite_ref-69}  

Main sights {#Main_sights}
--------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Main sights")\]  

### Ancient/archeological sites {#Ancient.2Farcheological_sites}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Ancient/archeological sites")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ankara_Castle.jpg/220px-Ankara_Castle.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_Castle.jpg) [Ankara castle and citadel](/wiki/Ankara_Castle "Ankara Castle") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/The_Roman_Theatre_of_Ancyra%2C_2nd_half_of_the_1st_century_AD_-_beg_of_the_2nd_century_AD%2C_Ankara%2C_Turkey_%2825743828343%29.jpg/220px-The_Roman_Theatre_of_Ancyra%2C_2nd_half_of_the_1st_century_AD_-_beg_of_the_2nd_century_AD%2C_Ankara%2C_Turkey_%2825743828343%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_Roman_Theatre_of_Ancyra,_2nd_half_of_the_1st_century_AD_-_beg_of_the_2nd_century_AD,_Ankara,_Turkey_(25743828343).jpg) [Theatre of Ancyra](/wiki/Antique_Rome_theatre_of_Ankara "Antique Rome theatre of Ankara") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/AugustusAnkara2.jpg/220px-AugustusAnkara2.jpg)](/wiki/File:AugustusAnkara2.jpg) At the [Monumentum Ancyranum](/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum "Monumentum Ancyranum") (*Temple of Augustus and Rome* ) in Ulus, the primary intact copy of [Res Gestae](/wiki/Res_Gestae_Divi_Augusti "Res Gestae Divi Augusti") written by the first Roman emperor [Augustus](/wiki/Augustus "Augustus") survives. [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Ankara_Thermen12.jpg/220px-Ankara_Thermen12.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_Thermen12.jpg) [Roman Baths of Ankara](/wiki/Roman_Baths_of_Ankara "Roman Baths of Ankara")  

#### Ankara Citadel {#Ankara_Citadel}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Ankara Citadel")\]

The foundations of the [Ankara castle and citadel](/wiki/Ankara_Castle "Ankara Castle") were laid by the Galatians on a prominent [lava](/wiki/Lava "Lava") outcrop ( [39°56′28″N 32°51′50″E﻿ / ﻿39.941°N 32.864°E﻿ / 39.941; 32.864](https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Ankara&params=39.941_N_32.864_E_type:landmark)), and the rest was completed by the Romans. The Byzantines and Seljuks further made restorations and additions. The area around and inside the citadel, being the oldest part of Ankara, contains many fine examples of traditional architecture. There are also recreational areas to relax. Many restored traditional Turkish houses inside the citadel area have found new life as restaurants, serving local cuisine.

The citadel was depicted in various Turkish banknotes during 1927--1952 and 1983--1989.^[\[66\]](#cite_note-70)^{#cite_ref-70}  

#### Roman Theater {#Roman_Theater}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Roman Theater")\]

The remains, the stage, and the backstage of the [Antique Rome theatre of Ankara](/wiki/Antique_Rome_theatre_of_Ankara "Antique Rome theatre of Ankara") can be seen outside [the castle](/wiki/Ankara_Castle "Ankara Castle"). Roman statues that were found here are exhibited in the [Museum of Anatolian Civilizations](/wiki/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations "Museum of Anatolian Civilizations"). The seating area is still under excavation.  

#### Temple of Augustus and Rome {#Temple_of_Augustus_and_Rome}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Temple of Augustus and Rome")\]  
Main article: [Temple of Augustus and Rome](/wiki/Temple_of_Augustus_and_Rome "Temple of Augustus and Rome")

The Augusteum,^[\[67\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911b953-71)^ now known as the Temple of Augustus and Rome, was built 25 20 BC following the conquest of Central Anatolia by the [Roman Empire](/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire"). Ancyra then formed the capital of the new [province](/wiki/Roman_province "Roman province") of [Galatia](/wiki/Galatia "Galatia"). After the death of [Augustus](/wiki/Augustus "Augustus") in AD 14, a copy of the text of the *[Res Gestae Divi Augusti](/wiki/Res_Gestae_Divi_Augusti "Res Gestae Divi Augusti")* (the *[Monumentum Ancyranum](/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum "Monumentum Ancyranum")* ) was inscribed on the interior of the temple's **pronaos** in Latin and a Greek translation on an exterior wall of the **cella** . The temple on the ancient acropolis of Ancyra was enlarged in the 2nd century and converted into a church in the 5th century. It is located in the Ulus quarter of the city. It was subsequently publicized by the [Austrian](/wiki/Austrian_Empire "Austrian Empire") ambassador [Ogier Ghiselin de Busbecq](/wiki/Ogier_Ghiselin_de_Busbecq "Ogier Ghiselin de Busbecq") in the 16th century.{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911b953_71-0}  

#### Roman Baths {#Roman_Baths}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Roman Baths")\]

The [Roman Baths of Ankara](/wiki/Roman_Baths_of_Ankara "Roman Baths of Ankara") have all the typical features of a classical [Roman bath complex](/wiki/Thermae "Thermae"): a *[frigidarium](/wiki/Frigidarium "Frigidarium")* (cold room), a *[tepidarium](/wiki/Tepidarium "Tepidarium")* (warm room) and a *[caldarium](/wiki/Caldarium "Caldarium")* (hot room). The baths were built during the reign of the Roman emperor [Caracalla](/wiki/Caracalla "Caracalla") in the early 3rd century to honor [Asclepios](/wiki/Asclepius "Asclepius"), the God of Medicine. Today, only the basement and first floors remain. It is situated in the Ulus quarter.  

#### Roman Road {#Roman_Road}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Roman Road")\]

The [Roman Road of Ankara](/wiki/Roman_Road_of_Ankara "Roman Road of Ankara") or *Cardo Maximus* was found in 1995 by Turkish archeologist Cevdet Bayburtluoğlu. It is 216 meters (709 feet) long and 6.7 meters (22.0 feet) wide. Many ancient artifacts were discovered during the excavations along the road and most of them are displayed at the [Museum of Anatolian Civilizations](/wiki/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations "Museum of Anatolian Civilizations").^[\[68\]](#cite_note-72)^^[\[69\]](#cite_note-Antik_Ankara-73)^{#cite_ref-Antik_Ankara_73-0}  

#### Column of Julian {#Column_of_Julian}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Column of Julian")\]

The Column of Julian or Julianus, now in the Ulus district, was erected in honor of the Roman emperor [Julian the Apostate](/wiki/Julian_the_Apostate "Julian the Apostate")'s visit to Ancyra in 362.  

### Mosques {#Mosques}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Mosques")\]  

#### Kocatepe Mosque {#Kocatepe_Mosque}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Kocatepe Mosque")\]  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/ANKARA_KOCATEPE_CAM%C4%B0%C4%B0.jpg/200px-ANKARA_KOCATEPE_CAM%C4%B0%C4%B0.jpg)](/wiki/File:ANKARA_KOCATEPE_CAM%C4%B0%C4%B0.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Ahmet_Hamdi_Akseki_Mosque%2C_Ankara_02.jpg/200px-Ahmet_Hamdi_Akseki_Mosque%2C_Ankara_02.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ahmet_Hamdi_Akseki_Mosque,_Ankara_02.jpg)  
**Top** : Kocatepe Mosque (1987)   
**Bottom**: Ahmet Hamdi Akseki Mosque (2013)

[Kocatepe Mosque](/wiki/Kocatepe_Mosque "Kocatepe Mosque") is the largest mosque in the city. Located in the Kocatepe quarter, it was constructed between 1967 and 1987 in classical [Ottoman style](/wiki/Ottoman_architecture "Ottoman architecture") with four minarets. Its size and prominent location have made it a landmark for the city.  

#### Ahmet Hamdi Akseki Mosque {#Ahmet_Hamdi_Akseki_Mosque}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Ahmet Hamdi Akseki Mosque")\]

Ahmet Hamdi Akseki Mosque is located near the Presidency of Religious Affairs on the [Eskişehir](/wiki/Eski%C5%9Fehir "Eskişehir") Road. Built in the Turkish neoclassical style, it is one of the largest new mosques in the city, completed and opened in 2013. It can accommodate 6 thousand people during general prayers, and up to 30 thousand people during funeral prayers. The mosque was decorated with [Anatolian Seljuk style](/wiki/Anatolian_Seljuk_architecture "Anatolian Seljuk architecture") patterns.^[\[70\]](#cite_note-74)^{#cite_ref-74}  

#### Yeni (Cenab Ahmet) Mosque {#Yeni_.28Cenab_Ahmet.29_Mosque}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Yeni (Cenab Ahmet) Mosque")\]

It is the largest Ottoman mosque in Ankara and was built by the famous architect Sinan in the 16th century. The mimber (pulpit) and mihrap (prayer niche) are of white marble, and the mosque itself is of Ankara stone, an example of very fine workmanship.  

#### Hacı Bayram Mosque {#Hac.C4.B1_Bayram_Mosque}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Hacı Bayram Mosque")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Haci_Bayram_Mosque_01.jpg/220px-Haci_Bayram_Mosque_01.jpg)](/wiki/File:Haci_Bayram_Mosque_01.jpg) [Hacı Bayram Mosque](/wiki/Hac%C4%B1_Bayram_Mosque "Hacı Bayram Mosque") (1428)

This mosque, in the Ulus quarter next to the [Temple of Augustus](/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum "Monumentum Ancyranum"), was built in the early 15th century in Seljuk style by an unknown architect. It was subsequently restored by architect [Mimar Sinan](/wiki/Mimar_Sinan "Mimar Sinan") in the 16th century, with [Kütahya](/wiki/K%C3%BCtahya "Kütahya") tiles being added in the 18th century. The mosque was built in honor of [Hacı Bayram-ı Veli](/wiki/Hac%C4%B1_Bayram-%C4%B1_Veli "Hacı Bayram-ı Veli"), whose tomb is next to the mosque, two years before his death (1427--28).^[\[71\]](#cite_note-75)^ The usable space inside this mosque is 437 m^2^ (4,704 sq ft) on the first floor and 263 m^2^ (2,831 sq ft) on the second floor.{#cite_ref-75}  

#### Ahi Elvan Mosque {#Ahi_Elvan_Mosque}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Ahi Elvan Mosque")\]

It was founded in the Ulus quarter near the Ankara Citadel and was constructed by the [Ahi fraternity](/wiki/Ahis "Ahis") during the late 14th and early 15th centuries. The finely carved walnut mimber (pulpit) is of particular interest.^[\[72\]](#cite_note-76)^{#cite_ref-76}  

#### Alâeddin Mosque {#Al.C3.A2eddin_Mosque}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Alâeddin Mosque")\]

The Alâeddin Mosque is the oldest mosque in Ankara. It has a [carved](/wiki/Wood_carving "Wood carving") [walnut](/wiki/Juglans "Juglans") [mimber](/wiki/Minbar "Minbar"), the inscription on which records that the mosque was completed in early [AH 574](/wiki/Islamic_calendar "Islamic calendar") (which corresponds to the summer of 1178 AD) and was built by the [Seljuk](/wiki/Seljuk_dynasty "Seljuk dynasty") prince Muhiddin Mesud Şah (died 1204), the [Bey](/wiki/Bey "Bey") of Ankara, who was the son of the [Anatolian Seljuk sultan](/wiki/Anatolian_Seljuk_Sultanate "Anatolian Seljuk Sultanate") [Kılıç Arslan II](/wiki/Kilij_Arslan_II "Kilij Arslan II") (reigned 1156--1192.)  

### Modern monuments {#Modern_monuments}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Modern monuments")\]

There are at least 50 monuments and reliefs throughout the city. Some notables are;  

#### Victory Monument {#Victory_Monument}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Victory Monument")\]  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Ankara_asv2021-10_img38_Victory_Monument.jpg/200px-Ankara_asv2021-10_img38_Victory_Monument.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_asv2021-10_img38_Victory_Monument.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Hittite_Sun_Course_Monument.jpg/200px-Hittite_Sun_Course_Monument.jpg)](/wiki/File:Hittite_Sun_Course_Monument.jpg)  
**Top** : Victory Monument (1927)   
**Bottom** : [Hittite Sun Course Monument](/wiki/Hittite_Sun_Course_Monument "Hittite Sun Course Monument") (1978)

The [Victory Monument](/wiki/Victory_Monument_(Ankara) "Victory Monument (Ankara)") ([Turkish](/wiki/Turkish_language "Turkish language"): *[Zafer Anıtı](https://tr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara_Zafer_An%C4%B1t%C4%B1 "tr:Ankara Zafer Anıtı")* ) was crafted by Austrian sculptor Heinrich Krippel in 1925 and was erected in 1927 at [Ulus Square](/wiki/Ulus_Square "Ulus Square"). The monument is made of [marble](/wiki/Marble "Marble") and [bronze](/wiki/Bronze "Bronze") and features an [equestrian statue](/wiki/Equestrian_statue "Equestrian statue") of [Mustafa Kemal Atatürk](/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk "Mustafa Kemal Atatürk"), who wears a Republic era modern military uniform, with the rank [Field Marshal](/wiki/Field_Marshal "Field Marshal").^[\[73\]](#cite_note-77)^{#cite_ref-77}  

#### Statue of Atatürk {#Statue_of_Atat.C3.BCrk}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Statue of Atatürk")\]

Located at Zafer(Victory) Square ([Turkish](/wiki/Turkish_language "Turkish language"): *Zafer Meydanı* ), the [marble](/wiki/Marble "Marble") and [bronze](/wiki/Bronze "Bronze") statue was crafted by the Italian sculptor [Pietro Canonica](/wiki/Pietro_Canonica "Pietro Canonica") in 1927 and depicts a standing Atatürk who wears a Republic era modern military uniform, with the rank [Field Marshal](/wiki/Field_Marshal "Field Marshal").  

#### Monument of Security {#Monument_of_Security}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Monument of Security")\]

The [Security Monument](/wiki/Security_Monument "Security Monument"), located in [Güvenpark](/wiki/G%C3%BCvenpark "Güvenpark") near Kızılay Square, was erected in 1935 and bears Atatürk's advice to his people: "Turk! Be proud, work hard, and believe in yourself." (There is debate on whether or not Atatürk actually said "Use your mind"(Turkish: öğün) instead of "Be proud"(Turkish: övün))^[\[74\]](#cite_note-78)^{#cite_ref-78}

The monument was depicted on the [reverse](/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse "Obverse and reverse") of the Turkish 5 [lira](/wiki/Turkish_lira "Turkish lira") banknote of 1937--1952^[\[75\]](#cite_note-79)^ and of the 1000 lira banknotes of 1939--1946.^[\[76\]](#cite_note-80)^{#cite_ref-80}  

#### Hatti Monument {#Hatti_Monument}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Hatti Monument")\]

Erected in 1978 at [Sıhhiye Square](/wiki/S%C4%B1hhiye_Square "Sıhhiye Square"), this impressive monument symbolizes the [Hatti](/wiki/Hattians "Hattians") Sun Disc (which was later adopted by the [Hittites](/wiki/Hittites "Hittites")) and commemorates Anatolia's earliest known civilization. The Hatti Sun Disc has been used in the previous logo of Ankara Metropolitan Municipality. It was also used in the previous logo of the Ministry of Culture \& Tourism.  

#### Korean War Monument {#Korean_War_Monument}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Korean War Monument")\]

The [Monument to Turkish Soldiers Fighting in Korea](/wiki/Monument_to_Turkish_Soldiers_Fighting_in_Korea "Monument to Turkish Soldiers Fighting in Korea") opened in 1973 to commemorate the veterans and martyrs of the [Turkish Brigade](/wiki/Turkish_Brigade "Turkish Brigade").^[\[77\]](#cite_note-81)^{#cite_ref-81}  

### Inns {#Inns}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Inns")\]  

#### Suluhan {#Suluhan}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Suluhan")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Ankara_september_2011_9289.jpg/220px-Ankara_september_2011_9289.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_september_2011_9289.jpg) [Çengelhan Rahmi M. Koç Museum](/wiki/%C3%87engelhan_Rahmi_M._Ko%C3%A7_Museum "Çengelhan Rahmi M. Koç Museum")'s courtyard has been covered with a glass roof.

[Suluhan](/wiki/Suluhan "Suluhan") is a historical Inn in Ankara. It is also called the *Hasanpaşa Han* . It is about 400 meters (1,300 ft) southeast of [Ulus Square](/wiki/Ulus_Square "Ulus Square") and situated in the Hacıdoğan neighborhood. According to the *vakfiye* (inscription) of the building, the Ottoman era *han* was commissioned by Hasan Pasha, a regional [beylerbey](/wiki/Beylerbey "Beylerbey"), and was constructed between 1508 and 1511, during the final years of the reign of Sultan [Bayezid II](/wiki/Bayezid_II "Bayezid II").^[\[78\]](#cite_note-Ank-82)^ There are 102 rooms (now shops) which face the two yards.^[\[79\]](#cite_note-83)^ In each room there is a window, a niche and a chimney.^[\[80\]](#cite_note-Ank2-84)^{#cite_ref-Ank2_84-0}  

#### Çengelhan Rahmi M. Koç Museum {#.C3.87engelhan_Rahmi_M._Ko.C3.A7_Museum}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Çengelhan Rahmi M. Koç Museum")\]

[Çengelhan Rahmi M. Koç Museum](/wiki/%C3%87engelhan_Rahmi_M._Ko%C3%A7_Museum "Çengelhan Rahmi M. Koç Museum") is a museum of industrial technology situated in [Çengel Han](https://tr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%87engel_Han "tr:Çengel Han"), an Ottoman era Inn which was completed in 1523, during the early years of the reign of Sultan [Suleiman the Magnificent](/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent "Suleiman the Magnificent"). The exhibits include industrial/technological artifacts from the 1850s onwards. There are also sections about Mustafa Kemal Atatürk, the founder of modern Turkey; Vehbi Koç, Rahmi Koç's father and one of the first industrialists of Turkey, and Ankara city.  

Shopping {#Shopping}
--------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Shopping")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Ankara_Armada_Al%C4%B1%C5%9Fveri%C5%9F_Merkezi.JPG/220px-Ankara_Armada_Al%C4%B1%C5%9Fveri%C5%9F_Merkezi.JPG)](/wiki/File:Ankara_Armada_Al%C4%B1%C5%9Fveri%C5%9F_Merkezi.JPG) Armada Shopping Mall

Foreign visitors to Ankara usually like to visit the old shops in *Çıkrıkçılar Yokuşu* (Weavers' Road) near Ulus, where myriad things ranging from traditional fabrics, hand-woven carpets and leather products can be found at bargain prices. *Bakırcılar Çarşısı* (Bazaar of Coppersmiths) is particularly popular, and many interesting items, not just of copper, can be found here like jewelry, carpets, costumes, antiques and embroidery. Up the hill to the castle gate, there are many shops selling a huge and fresh collection of spices, [dried fruits](/wiki/Dried_fruit "Dried fruit"), nuts, and other produce.
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Ankara_asv2021-10_img15_Atakule.jpg/170px-Ankara_asv2021-10_img15_Atakule.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_asv2021-10_img15_Atakule.jpg) [Atakule Tower](/wiki/Atakule "Atakule") and Atrium Shopping Mall

Modern shopping areas are mostly found in [Kızılay](/wiki/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay,_Ankara "Kızılay, Ankara"), or on Tunalı Hilmi Avenue, including the modern mall of [Karum](/wiki/List_of_shopping_malls_in_Turkey#Ankara "List of shopping malls in Turkey") (named after the ancient [Assyrian](/wiki/Assyria "Assyria") merchant colonies called [*Kârum*](/wiki/K%C3%BCltepe#Kârum_Kaneš "Kültepe") that were established in [central](/wiki/Central_Anatolia_Region "Central Anatolia Region") [Anatolia](/wiki/Anatolia "Anatolia") at the beginning of the [2nd millennium BC](/wiki/2nd_millennium_BC "2nd millennium BC")) which is located towards the end of the Avenue; and in [Çankaya](/wiki/%C3%87ankaya,_Ankara "Çankaya, Ankara"), the quarter with the highest elevation in the city. [Atakule Tower](/wiki/Atakule "Atakule") next to [Atrium Mall](/wiki/Atakule#Atrium_shopping_mall "Atakule") in Çankaya has views over Ankara and also has a [revolving restaurant](/wiki/Revolving_restaurant "Revolving restaurant") at the top. The symbol of the [Armada Shopping Mall](/wiki/List_of_shopping_malls_in_Turkey#Ankara "List of shopping malls in Turkey") is an [anchor](/wiki/Anchor "Anchor"), and there's a large anchor monument at its entrance, as a reference to the ancient Greek name of the city, Ἄγκυρα (Ánkyra), which means anchor. Likewise, the anchor monument is also related with the Spanish name of the mall, Armada, which means [naval fleet](/wiki/Naval_fleet "Naval fleet").
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Ankara_Sheraton_Oteli_%282%29.jpg/220px-Ankara_Sheraton_Oteli_%282%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_Sheraton_Oteli_(2).jpg) [Sheraton Ankara](/wiki/Sheraton_Ankara "Sheraton Ankara") and Karum Shopping Mall

As Ankara started expanding westward in the 1970s, several modern, suburbia-style developments, mini-cities and business districts such as [Söğütözü](/wiki/S%C3%B6%C4%9F%C3%BCt%C3%B6z%C3%BC "Söğütözü") began to rise along the western highway, also known as the [Eskişehir](/wiki/Eski%C5%9Fehir "Eskişehir") Road. The *Armada* , *CEPA* and *Kentpark* malls on the highway, the *Galleria* , *Arcadium* and *Gordion* in Ümitköy, and a huge mall, *Real* in Bilkent Center, offer North American and European style shopping opportunities (these places can be reached through the Eskişehir Highway.) There is also the newly expanded *[ANKAmall](/wiki/ANKAmall "ANKAmall")* at the outskirts, on the Istanbul Highway, which houses most of the well-known international brands. This mall is the largest throughout the Ankara region. In 2014, a few more shopping malls were open in Ankara. They are *Next Level* and *Taurus* on the Boulevard of [Mevlana](/wiki/Mevlana "Mevlana") (also known as [Konya](/wiki/Konya "Konya") Road).  

Culture {#Culture}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Culture")\]  

### The arts {#The_arts}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: The arts")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Ankara_asv2021-10_img54_view_from_Gen%C3%A7lik_Park_Ferris_wheel.jpg/250px-Ankara_asv2021-10_img54_view_from_Gen%C3%A7lik_Park_Ferris_wheel.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_asv2021-10_img54_view_from_Gen%C3%A7lik_Park_Ferris_wheel.jpg) [Ankara Opera House](/wiki/Ankara_Opera_House "Ankara Opera House") of the Turkish State Opera and Ballet (1933) [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/CSOAdaAnkaraExterior.jpg/170px-CSOAdaAnkaraExterior.jpg)](/wiki/File:CSOAdaAnkaraExterior.jpg) [CSO Ada Ankara](/wiki/CSO_Ada_Ankara "CSO Ada Ankara") serves as the Presidential Symphony Orchestra Concert Hall.

[Turkish State Opera and Ballet](/wiki/Turkish_State_Opera_and_Ballet "Turkish State Opera and Ballet"), the national directorate of opera and ballet companies of Turkey, has its headquarters in Ankara, and serves the city with three venues:

* [Ankara Opera House](/wiki/Ankara_Opera_House "Ankara Opera House") (*Opera Sahnesi* , also known as *Büyük Tiyatro*) is the largest of the three venues for opera and ballet in Ankara.

#### Music {#Music}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=44 "Edit section: Music")\]

Ankara is host to five classical music orchestras:

* [Presidential Symphony Orchestra](/wiki/Presidential_Symphony_Orchestra "Presidential Symphony Orchestra") (Turkish Presidential Symphony Orchestra)
* [Bilkent Symphony Orchestra](/wiki/Bilkent_Symphony_Orchestra "Bilkent Symphony Orchestra") (BSO) is a major symphony orchestra of Turkey.
* [Hacettepe Symphony Orchestra](/wiki/Hacettepe_Symphony_Orchestra "Hacettepe Symphony Orchestra") was founded in 2003 and directed by Erol Erdinç
* Başkent Oda Orkestrası (Chamber Orchestra of the Capital)^[\[81\]](#cite_note-85)^{#cite_ref-85}

There are four concert halls in the city:

* [CSO Concert Hall](/wiki/CSO_Concert_Hall "CSO Concert Hall")
* [Bilkent Concert Hall](/wiki/Bilkent_Concert_Hall "Bilkent Concert Hall") is a performing arts center in Ankara. It is located in the Bilkent University campus.
* [MEB Şura Salonu](/wiki/MEB_%C5%9Eura_Salonu "MEB Şura Salonu") (also known as the Festival Hall), It is noted for its tango performances.
* [Çankaya Çağdaş Sanatlar Merkezi Concert Hall](/wiki/%C3%87ankaya_%C3%87a%C4%9Fda%C5%9F_Sanatlar_Merkezi_Concert_Hall "Çankaya Çağdaş Sanatlar Merkezi Concert Hall") was founded in 1994.

The city has been host to several well-established, annual theater, music, film festivals:

* [Ankara International Music Festival](/wiki/Ankara_International_Music_Festival "Ankara International Music Festival"), a music festival organized in the Turkish capital presenting classical music and ballet programs.

Ankara also has a number of concert venues such as *Eskiyeni* , *[IF Performance Hall](/wiki/IF_Performance_Hall "IF Performance Hall")* , *[Jolly Joker](/wiki/Jolly_Joker_(venues_chain) "Jolly Joker (venues chain)")* , *Kite* , *Nefes Bar* , and *Route*, which host the live performances and events of popular musicians.  

#### Theater {#Theater}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: Theater")\]

The [Turkish State Theatres](/wiki/Turkish_State_Theatres "Turkish State Theatres") also has its head office in Ankara and runs the following stages in the city:  
* [125. Yıl Çayyolu Sahnesi](/wiki/125._Y%C4%B1l_%C3%87ayyolu_Sahnesi "125. Yıl Çayyolu Sahnesi")
* [Büyük Tiyatro](https://tr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara_Devlet_Tiyatrosu "tr:Ankara Devlet Tiyatrosu"),
* [Küçük Tiyatro](/wiki/K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_Tiyatro "Küçük Tiyatro"),
* [Şinasi Sahnesi](/wiki/%C5%9Einasi_Sahnesi "Şinasi Sahnesi"),
* [Akün Sahnesi](/wiki/Ak%C3%BCn_Sahnesi "Akün Sahnesi"),
* [Altındağ Tiyatrosu](/wiki/Alt%C4%B1nda%C4%9F_Tiyatrosu "Altındağ Tiyatrosu"),
* [İrfan Şahinbaş Atölye Sahnesi](/wiki/%C4%B0rfan_%C5%9Eahinba%C5%9F_At%C3%B6lye_Sahnesi "İrfan Şahinbaş Atölye Sahnesi"),
* [Oda Tiyatrosu](/wiki/Oda_Tiyatrosu "Oda Tiyatrosu"),
* [Mahir Canova Sahnesi](/wiki/Mahir_Canova_Sahnesi "Mahir Canova Sahnesi"),
* [Muhsin Ertuğrul Sahnesi](/wiki/Muhsin_Ertu%C4%9Frul_Sahnesi "Muhsin Ertuğrul Sahnesi").

In addition, the city is served by several private theater companies, among which [Ankara Sanat Tiyatrosu](https://tr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ankara_Sanat_Tiyatrosu "tr:Ankara Sanat Tiyatrosu"), who have their own stage in the city center, is a notable example.  

### Museums {#Museums}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Museums")\]

There are about 50 museums in the city. Some notables include;  

#### Museum of Anatolian Civilizations {#Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: Museum of Anatolian Civilizations")\]

The [Museum of Anatolian Civilizations](/wiki/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations "Museum of Anatolian Civilizations") (*Anadolu Medeniyetleri Müzesi* ) is situated at the entrance of the [Ankara Castle](/wiki/Ankara_Castle "Ankara Castle"). It is an old 15th century [bedesten](/wiki/Bedesten "Bedesten") (covered bazaar)^[\[82\]](#cite_note-86)^ that has been restored and now houses a collection of [Paleolithic](/wiki/Paleolithic "Paleolithic"), [Neolithic](/wiki/Neolithic "Neolithic"), [Hatti](/wiki/Hittite_empire "Hittite empire"), [Hittite](/wiki/Hittites "Hittites"), [Phrygian](/wiki/Phrygia "Phrygia"), [Urartian](/wiki/Urartu "Urartu") and [Roman](/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire") works as well as a major section dedicated to [Lydian](/wiki/Lydia "Lydia") treasures.{#cite_ref-86}  

#### Anıtkabir {#An.C4.B1tkabir}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=48 "Edit section: Anıtkabir")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/An%C4%B1tkabir_ziyareti.jpeg/220px-An%C4%B1tkabir_ziyareti.jpeg)](/wiki/File:An%C4%B1tkabir_ziyareti.jpeg) [Atatürk's Mausoleum](/wiki/An%C4%B1tkabir "Anıtkabir") is the mausoleum of Mustafa Kemal Atatürk, founder of the Republic of Turkey.

[Anıtkabir](/wiki/An%C4%B1tkabir "Anıtkabir") is located on an imposing hill, which forms the *Anıttepe* quarter of the city, where the mausoleum of [Mustafa Kemal Atatürk](/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk "Mustafa Kemal Atatürk"), founder of the Republic of Turkey, stands. Completed in 1953, it is a fusion of ancient and modern architectural styles. An adjacent museum houses a wax statue of Atatürk, his writings, letters and personal items, as well as an exhibition of photographs recording important moments in his life and during the establishment of the Republic. Anıtkabir is open every day, while the adjacent museum is open every day except Mondays.  

#### Ankara Aviation Museum {#Ankara_Aviation_Museum}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=49 "Edit section: Ankara Aviation Museum")\]

[Ankara Aviation Museum](/wiki/Ankara_Aviation_Museum "Ankara Aviation Museum") (*Hava Kuvvetleri Müzesi Komutanlığı* ) is located near the Istanbul Road in Etimesgut. The museum opened to the public in September 1998.^[\[83\]](#cite_note-87)^ It is home to various missiles, avionics, aviation materials and aircraft that have served in the [Turkish Air Force](/wiki/Turkish_Air_Force "Turkish Air Force") (e.g. combat aircraft such as the [F-86 Sabre](/wiki/F-86_Sabre "F-86 Sabre"), [F-100 Super Sabre](/wiki/F-100_Super_Sabre "F-100 Super Sabre"), [F-102 Delta Dagger](/wiki/F-102_Delta_Dagger "F-102 Delta Dagger"), [F-104 Starfighter](/wiki/F-104_Starfighter "F-104 Starfighter"), [F-5 Freedom Fighter](/wiki/Northrop_F-5 "Northrop F-5"), [F-4 Phantom](/wiki/F-4_Phantom_II "F-4 Phantom II"); and cargo planes such as the [Transall C-160](/wiki/Transall_C-160 "Transall C-160").) Also a Hungarian [MiG-21](/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21 "Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-21"), a Pakistani [MiG-19](/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-19 "Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-19"), and a Bulgarian [MiG-17](/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-17 "Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-17") are on display at the museum.{#cite_ref-87}  

#### Cer Modern {#Cer_Modern}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=50 "Edit section: Cer Modern")\]

Cer Modern is the modern-arts museum of Ankara, inaugurated on 1 April 2010. It is situated in the renovated building of the historic [TCDD](/wiki/Turkish_State_Railways "Turkish State Railways") Cer Atölyeleri, formerly a workshop of the [Turkish State Railways](/wiki/Turkish_State_Railways "Turkish State Railways"). The museum incorporates the largest exhibition hall in Turkey. The museum holds periodic exhibitions of modern and contemporary art as well as hosting other contemporary arts events.  

#### Ankara Ethnography Museum {#Ankara_Ethnography_Museum}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=51 "Edit section: Ankara Ethnography Museum")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Ethnography_Museum_of_Ankara.jpg/220px-Ethnography_Museum_of_Ankara.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ethnography_Museum_of_Ankara.jpg) [Ethnography Museum of Ankara](/wiki/Ethnography_Museum_of_Ankara "Ethnography Museum of Ankara")

[Ankara Ethnography Museum](/wiki/Ethnography_Museum_of_Ankara "Ethnography Museum of Ankara") (*Etnoğrafya Müzesi* ) is located opposite to the [Ankara Opera House](/wiki/Ankara_Opera_House "Ankara Opera House") on Talat Paşa Boulevard, in the Ulus district. There is a fine collection of folkloric items, as well as artifacts from the Seljuk and Ottoman periods. In front of the museum building, there is a [marble](/wiki/Marble "Marble") and [bronze](/wiki/Bronze "Bronze") [equestrian statue](/wiki/Equestrian_statue "Equestrian statue") of [Mustafa Kemal Atatürk](/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk "Mustafa Kemal Atatürk") (who wears a Republic era modern military uniform, with the rank [Field Marshal](/wiki/Field_Marshal "Field Marshal")) which was crafted in 1927^[\[84\]](#cite_note-88)^ by the Italian sculptor [Pietro Canonica](/wiki/Pietro_Canonica "Pietro Canonica").{#cite_ref-88}  

#### Mehmet Akif Literature Museum Library {#Mehmet_Akif_Literature_Museum_Library}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=52 "Edit section: Mehmet Akif Literature Museum Library")\]

The [Mehmet Akif Literature Museum Library](/wiki/Mehmet_Akif_Literature_Museum_Library "Mehmet Akif Literature Museum Library") is an important literary museum and archive opened in 2011 and dedicated to [Mehmet Akif Ersoy](/wiki/Mehmet_Akif_Ersoy "Mehmet Akif Ersoy") (1873--1936), the poet of the [Turkish National Anthem](/wiki/Turkish_National_Anthem "Turkish National Anthem").  

#### METU Science and Technology Museum / Archaeology Museum {#METU_Science_and_Technology_Museum_.2F_Archaeology_Museum}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=53 "Edit section: METU Science and Technology Museum / Archaeology Museum")\]

Both the [METU Science and Technology Museum](/wiki/METU_Science_and_Technology_Museum "METU Science and Technology Museum") (*ODTÜ Bilim ve Teknoloji Müzesi* ) and the Archaeology Museum (*ODTÜ Arkeoloji Müzesi* ) are located inside the [Middle East Technical University](/wiki/METU "METU") campus.  

#### Republic \& War of Independence Museum {#Republic_.26_War_of_Independence_Museum}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=54 "Edit section: Republic & War of Independence Museum")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Ankara_asv2021-10_img45_Cumhuriyet_Street_on_29Oct.jpg/220px-Ankara_asv2021-10_img45_Cumhuriyet_Street_on_29Oct.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_asv2021-10_img45_Cumhuriyet_Street_on_29Oct.jpg) The [War of Independence Museum](/wiki/War_of_Independence_Museum "War of Independence Museum"), used as the first Turkish Grand National Assembly building

Both the [Republic Museum](/wiki/Republic_Museum "Republic Museum") and [War of Independence Museum](/wiki/War_of_Independence_Museum "War of Independence Museum") are located on [Ulus Square](/wiki/Ulus_Square "Ulus Square"). They were originally the first and second Parliament building (TBMM) of the Republic of Turkey, respectively. The War of Independence was planned and directed here as recorded in various photographs and items presently on exhibition. In another display, [wax figures](/wiki/Wax_sculpture "Wax sculpture") of former presidents of the Republic of Turkey are on exhibit.  

#### State Art and Sculpture Museum {#State_Art_and_Sculpture_Museum}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=55 "Edit section: State Art and Sculpture Museum")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Ankara_asv2021-10_img64_Arts_and_Sculpture_Museum.jpg/220px-Ankara_asv2021-10_img64_Arts_and_Sculpture_Museum.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_asv2021-10_img64_Arts_and_Sculpture_Museum.jpg) [State Art and Sculpture Museum](/wiki/State_Art_and_Sculpture_Museum "State Art and Sculpture Museum")

The [State Art and Sculpture Museum](/wiki/State_Art_and_Sculpture_Museum "State Art and Sculpture Museum") (*Resim-Heykel Müzesi* ) which opened to the public in 1980^[\[85\]](#cite_note-89)^ is close to the Ethnography Museum and houses a rich collection of Turkish art from the late 19th century to the present day. There are also galleries which host guest exhibitions.{#cite_ref-89}  

#### TCDD Open Air Steam Locomotive Museum {#TCDD_Open_Air_Steam_Locomotive_Museum}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=56 "Edit section: TCDD Open Air Steam Locomotive Museum")\]

The [TCDD Open Air Steam Locomotive Museum](/wiki/TCDD_Open_Air_Steam_Locomotive_Museum "TCDD Open Air Steam Locomotive Museum") is an [open-air museum](/wiki/Open-air_museum "Open-air museum") which traces the history of [steam locomotives](/wiki/Steam_locomotive "Steam locomotive").  

### Sports {#Sports}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=57 "Edit section: Sports")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Ankara_asv2021-10_img20_Ankara_Arena.jpg/220px-Ankara_asv2021-10_img20_Ankara_Arena.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ankara_asv2021-10_img20_Ankara_Arena.jpg) [Ankara Arena](/wiki/Ankara_Arena "Ankara Arena")

As with all other cities of Turkey, football is the most popular sport in Ankara. The city currently has one [football club](/wiki/Football_team "Football team") competing in the [Turkish Süper Lig](/wiki/S%C3%BCper_Lig "Süper Lig"): [Ankaragücü](/wiki/MKE_Ankarag%C3%BCc%C3%BC "MKE Ankaragücü"), founded in 1910, is the oldest club in Ankara and is associated with Ankara's military arsenal manufacturing company [MKE](/wiki/Mechanical_and_Chemical_Industry_Corporation "Mechanical and Chemical Industry Corporation"). They were the [Turkish Cup](/wiki/Turkish_Cup "Turkish Cup") winners in 1972 and 1981. [Gençlerbirliği](/wiki/Gen%C3%A7lerbirli%C4%9Fi_S.K. "Gençlerbirliği S.K."), founded in 1923, play in the [TFF First League](/wiki/TFF_First_League "TFF First League") and are known as the *Ankara Gale* or the *Poppies* because of their colors: red and black. They were the Turkish Cup winners in 1987 and 2001. [Ankara Keçiörengücü](/wiki/Ankara_Ke%C3%A7i%C3%B6reng%C3%BCc%C3%BC "Ankara Keçiörengücü") also currently play in the [TFF First League](/wiki/TFF_First_League "TFF First League"). [Büyükşehir Belediye Ankaraspor](/wiki/B%C3%BCy%C3%BCk%C5%9Fehir_Belediye_Ankaraspor "Büyükşehir Belediye Ankaraspor") also played in the Süper Lig until 2010, when they were expelled. The club was reconstituted in 2014 as [Osmanlıspor](/wiki/Osmanl%C4%B1spor "Osmanlıspor") but have since returned to their old identity as [Ankaraspor](/wiki/Ankaraspor "Ankaraspor"). Ankaraspor currently play in the [TFF Second League](/wiki/TFF_Second_League "TFF Second League") at the Etimesgut Belediyesi Atatürk Stadium. Gençlerbirliği's B team, [Hacettepe S.K.](/wiki/Hacettepe_S.K. "Hacettepe S.K.") (formerly known as Gençlerbirliği OFTAŞ) played in the Süper Lig but folded in 2023. [Ankara Demirspor](/wiki/Ankara_Demirspor "Ankara Demirspor") and [Etimesgut Belediyespor](/wiki/Etimesgut_Belediyespor "Etimesgut Belediyespor") also play in the [TFF Second League](/wiki/TFF_Second_League "TFF Second League"). Ankara has a large number of minor teams, playing at regional levels, including [Çankaya FK](/wiki/%C3%87ankaya_FK "Çankaya FK"), Altındağspor,^[\[86\]](#cite_note-tff-90)^ [Mamak FK](/wiki/Mamak_FK "Mamak FK"), Çubukspor, and Bağlumspor.{#cite_ref-tff_90-0}

In the [Turkish Basketball Super League](/wiki/Basketbol_S%C3%BCper_Ligi "Basketbol Süper Ligi"), Ankara is represented by [Türk Telekom B.K.](/wiki/T%C3%BCrk_Telekom_B.K. "Türk Telekom B.K."), who play at the [Ankara Arena](/wiki/Ankara_Arena "Ankara Arena"). [TED Ankara Kolejliler](/wiki/TED_Ankara_Kolejliler "TED Ankara Kolejliler"), MKE Ankaragücü, and [OGM Ormanspor](/wiki/OGM_Ormanspor "OGM Ormanspor") play in the second-tier [Turkish First League](/wiki/T%C3%BCrkiye_Basketbol_Ligi "Türkiye Basketbol Ligi"). Türk Telekom became the fourth team in the country's history to participate in [EuroCup](/wiki/EuroCup_Basketball "EuroCup Basketball") finals ([22-23](/wiki/2022%E2%80%9323_EuroCup_Basketball "2022–23 EuroCup Basketball")).

[Halkbank Ankara](/wiki/Halkbank_Ankara "Halkbank Ankara") is the leading domestic powerhouse in men's volleyball, having won many championships and cups in the [Turkish Men's Volleyball League](/wiki/Turkish_Men%27s_Volleyball_League "Turkish Men's Volleyball League") and even the [CEV Cup](/wiki/CEV_Cup "CEV Cup") in 2013.

[Ankara Buz Pateni Sarayı](/wiki/Ankara_Ice_Palace "Ankara Ice Palace") is where the [ice skating](/wiki/Ice_skating "Ice skating") and [ice hockey](/wiki/Ice_hockey "Ice hockey") competitions take place in the city.

There are many popular spots for [skateboarding](/wiki/Skateboarding "Skateboarding") which is active in the city since the 1980s. Skaters in Ankara usually meet in the park near the [Grand National Assembly of Turkey](/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey "Grand National Assembly of Turkey").

The 2012-built [THF Sport Hall](/wiki/THF_Sport_Hall "THF Sport Hall") hosts the [Handball Super League](/wiki/Turkish_Handball_Super_League "Turkish Handball Super League") and [Women's Handball Super League](/wiki/Turkish_Women%27s_Handball_Super_League "Turkish Women's Handball Super League") matches scheduled in Ankara.^[\[87\]](#cite_note-91)^{#cite_ref-91}  

Parks {#Parks}
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=58 "Edit section: Parks")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Se%C4%9Fmenler_Park%C4%B1.jpg/220px-Se%C4%9Fmenler_Park%C4%B1.jpg)](/wiki/File:Se%C4%9Fmenler_Park%C4%B1.jpg) Seğmenler Park [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/G%C3%B6ksupark_Ankara_-_21821118323.jpg/220px-G%C3%B6ksupark_Ankara_-_21821118323.jpg)](/wiki/File:G%C3%B6ksupark_Ankara_-_21821118323.jpg) [Göksu Park](/wiki/G%C3%B6ksu_Park "Göksu Park")

Ankara has many parks and open spaces mainly established in the early years of the Republic and well maintained and expanded thereafter. The most important of these parks are: [Gençlik Parkı](/wiki/Gen%C3%A7lik_Park%C4%B1 "Gençlik Parkı") (houses an [amusement park](/wiki/Amusement_park "Amusement park") with a large pond for rowing), the [Botanical garden](/wiki/Botanical_garden "Botanical garden"), Seğmenler Park, Anayasa Park, [Kuğulu Park](/wiki/Ku%C4%9Fulu_Park "Kuğulu Park") (famous for the swans received as a gift from the [Chinese](/wiki/PRC "PRC") government), [Abdi İpekçi](/wiki/Abdi_%C4%B0pek%C3%A7i "Abdi İpekçi") Park, [Esertepe Parkı](/wiki/Esertepe_Park%C4%B1 "Esertepe Parkı"), Güven Park (see above for the monument), Kurtuluş Park (has an ice-skating rink), [Altınpark](/wiki/Alt%C4%B1npark "Altınpark") (also a prominent exposition/fair area), Harikalar Diyarı (claimed to be Biggest Park of Europe inside city borders) and Göksu Park. [Dikmen Vadisi](/wiki/Dikmen_Vadisi "Dikmen Vadisi") (Dikmen Valley) is a 70 hectares (170 acres) park and recreation area situated in Çankaya district.

Gençlik Park was depicted on the [reverse](/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse "Obverse and reverse") of the Turkish 100 [lira](/wiki/Turkish_lira "Turkish lira") banknotes of 1952--1976.^[\[88\]](#cite_note-92)^{#cite_ref-92}

[Atatürk Forest Farm and Zoo](/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk_Forest_Farm_and_Zoo "Atatürk Forest Farm and Zoo") (*Atatürk Orman Çiftliği* ) is an expansive recreational farming area which houses a [zoo](/wiki/Zoo "Zoo"), several small agricultural farms, [greenhouses](/wiki/Greenhouse "Greenhouse"), restaurants, a [dairy farm](/wiki/Dairy_farming "Dairy farming") and a brewery. It is a pleasant place to spend a day with family, be it for having picnics, hiking, biking or simply enjoying good food and nature. There is also an exact replica of the house where Atatürk was born in 1881, in [Thessaloniki](/wiki/Thessaloniki "Thessaloniki"), Greece. Visitors to the "Çiftlik" (farm) as it is affectionately called by Ankarans, can sample such famous products of the farm such as old-fashioned beer and [ice cream](/wiki/Ice_cream "Ice cream"), fresh [dairy products](/wiki/Dairy_product "Dairy product") and meat rolls/kebabs made on charcoal, at a traditional restaurant (*Merkez Lokantası*, Central Restaurant), cafés and other establishments scattered around the farm.

Fauna {#Fauna}
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=61 "Edit section: Fauna")\]  

### Angora cat {#Angora_cat}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=62 "Edit section: Angora cat")\]  
Main article: [Turkish Angora](/wiki/Turkish_Angora "Turkish Angora")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg/180px-Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg)](/wiki/File:Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg) [Angora cat](/wiki/Turkish_Angora "Turkish Angora") with odd eyes (heterochromia), which is common among the Angoras

Ankara is home to a world-famous domestic [cat breed](/wiki/Cat_breed "Cat breed") -- the [Turkish Angora](/wiki/Turkish_Angora "Turkish Angora"), called *Ankara kedisi* (Ankara cat) in Turkish. Turkish Angoras are one of the ancient, naturally occurring cat breeds, having originated in Ankara and its surrounding region in central Anatolia.

They mostly have a white, silky, medium to long length coat, no undercoat and a fine bone structure. There seems to be a connection between the Angora Cats and [Persians](/wiki/Persian_(cat) "Persian (cat)"), and the Turkish Angora is also a distant cousin of the [Turkish Van](/wiki/Turkish_Van "Turkish Van"). Although they are known for their shimmery white coat, there are more than twenty varieties including black, blue and reddish fur. They come in [tabby](/wiki/Tabby_cat "Tabby cat") and tabby-white, along with smoke varieties, and are in every color other than pointed, lavender, and cinnamon (all of which would indicate breeding to an outcross.)

Eyes may be blue, green, or amber, or even one blue and one amber or green. The [W gene](/wiki/Cat_coat_genetics#White_spotting_and_epistatic_white "Cat coat genetics") which is responsible for the white coat and blue eye is closely related to the hearing ability, and the presence of a blue eye can indicate that the cat is deaf to the side the blue eye is located. However, a great many blue and [odd-eyed](/wiki/Odd-eyed_cat "Odd-eyed cat") white cats have normal hearing, and even deaf cats lead a very normal life if kept indoors.

Ears are pointed and large, eyes are almond shaped and the head is massive with a two plane profile. Another characteristic is the tail, which is often kept parallel to the back.  

### Angora goat {#Angora_goat}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=63 "Edit section: Angora goat")\]  
Main article: [Angora goat](/wiki/Angora_goat "Angora goat")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Angora1.JPG/180px-Angora1.JPG)](/wiki/File:Angora1.JPG) Angora goat

The [Angora goat](/wiki/Angora_goat "Angora goat") ([Turkish](/wiki/Turkish_language "Turkish language"): *Ankara keçisi* ) is a breed of [domestic goat](/wiki/Goat "Goat") that originated in Ankara and its surrounding region in central Anatolia.^[\[89\]](#cite_note-Ekarius-93)^{#cite_ref-Ekarius_93-0}

This breed was first mentioned in the time of [Moses](/wiki/Moses "Moses"), roughly in 1500 BC.^[\[90\]](#cite_note-94)^ The first Angora goats were brought to Europe by [Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor](/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor "Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor"), about 1554, but, like later imports, were not very successful. Angora goats were first introduced in the United States in 1849 by James P. Davis. Seven adult goats were a gift from Sultan [Abdülmecid I](/wiki/Abd%C3%BClmecid_I "Abdülmecid I") in appreciation for his services and advice on the raising of cotton.{#cite_ref-94}

The [fleece](/wiki/Pile_(textile) "Pile (textile)") taken from an Angora goat is called [mohair](/wiki/Mohair "Mohair"). A single goat produces between five and eight kilograms (11 and 18 [pounds](/wiki/Pound_(mass) "Pound (mass)")) of hair per year. Angoras are shorn twice a year, unlike [sheep](/wiki/Domestic_sheep "Domestic sheep"), which are shorn only once. Angoras have high nutritional requirements due to their rapid hair growth. A poor quality diet will curtail mohair development. The United States, [Turkey](/wiki/Turkey "Turkey"), and South Africa are the top producers of mohair.

For a long period of time, Angora goats were bred for their white coat. In 1998, the Colored Angora Goat Breeders Association was set up to promote breeding of colored Angoras. Today, Angora goats produce white, black (deep black to greys and silver), red (the color fades significantly as the goat gets older), and brownish fiber.

Angora goats were depicted on the [reverse](/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse "Obverse and reverse") of the Turkish 50 [lira](/wiki/Turkish_lira "Turkish lira") banknotes of 1938--1952.^[\[91\]](#cite_note-95)^{#cite_ref-95}  

### Angora rabbit {#Angora_rabbit}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Ankara&action=edit&section=64 "Edit section: Angora rabbit")\]  
Main article: [Angora rabbit](/wiki/Angora_rabbit "Angora rabbit")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg/180px-Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg)](/wiki/File:Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg) Angora rabbit

The [Angora rabbit](/wiki/Angora_rabbit "Angora rabbit") ([Turkish](/wiki/Turkish_language "Turkish language"): *Ankara tavşanı* ) is a variety of domestic rabbit bred for its long, soft hair. The Angora is one of the oldest types of domestic rabbit, originating in Ankara and its surrounding region in central Anatolia, along with the [Angora cat](/wiki/Turkish_Angora "Turkish Angora") and [Angora goat](/wiki/Angora_goat "Angora goat"). The rabbits were popular pets with French royalty in the mid-18th century, and spread to other parts of Europe by the end of the century. They first appeared in the United States in the early 20th century. They are bred largely for their long [Angora wool](/wiki/Angora_wool "Angora wool"), which may be removed by [shearing](/wiki/Sheep_shearing "Sheep shearing"), combing, or [plucking](/wiki/Plucking_(hair_removal) "Plucking (hair removal)") (gently pulling loose wool).

Angoras are bred mainly for their wool because it is silky and soft. They have a humorous appearance, as they oddly resemble a fur ball. Most are calm and docile but should be handled carefully. Grooming is necessary to prevent the fiber from matting and felting on the rabbit. A condition called "wool block" is common in Angora rabbits and should be treated quickly.^[\[92\]](#cite_note-96)^ Sometimes they are shorn in the summer as the long fur can cause the rabbits to overheat.{#cite_ref-96}

1. **[\^](#cite_ref-5)** Ankara Province / Metropolitan municipality \[25,632 km² (including lake)^[\[1\]](#cite_note-1)^^[\[2\]](#cite_note-2)^^[\[3\]](#cite_note-Gölbaşı1-3)^ / 24,521 km² (excluding lake) according to the Turkish Statistical Institute -- TÜİK\], is a province (*il*) of Turkey which has [25 districts](/wiki/Ankara_Province#Districts "Ankara Province") (*ilçe*) and 9 of these districts form the urban area of Ankara city (4,130.2 km² including lake).^[\[4\]](#cite_note-citypopulation.de-4)^  
   Altındağ = 158.2 km²   
   Çankaya = 454.2 km²   
   Etimesgut = 283.2 km²   
   Gölbaşı = 1,508.6 km² (a small area is part of the city proper)^[\[3\]](#cite_note-Gölbaşı1-3)^  
   Keçiören = 152.2 km²   
   Mamak = 345.7 km²   
   Pursaklar = 133.7 km²   
   Sincan = 862.3 km²   
   Yenimahalle = 232.1 km²{#cite_ref-Gölbaşı1_3-1}
{#cite_note-5}
